Utah Code Annotated - Title 75A - Fiduciaries
=============================================

Utah Code Annotated - Title 75A - Chapter 1 - Fiduciaries
*********************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-101 Reserved for title definitions.
---------------------------------------------------------------
Reserved.

Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-102 Transition clause.
--------------------------------------------------
If, at the time a power of attorney, a power of appointment, an advanced health care directive, or another legal document was executed, the document contained a correct citation to a provision in Title 22, Fiduciaries and Trusts, and Title 75, Utah Uniform Probate Code, that, after the execution of the document, was renumbered and amended for inclusion in this title, that citation is a valid citation to the same provision in this title.

Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-201 Definitions for part.
-----------------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-201(1): "Fiduciary" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-201(1)(a): a trustee under any trust, expressed, implied, resulting or constructive;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-201(1)(b): an executor;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-201(1)(c): an administrator;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-201(1)(d): a guardian;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-201(1)(e): a conservator;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-201(1)(f): a curator;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-201(1)(g): a receiver;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-201(1)(h): a trustee in bankruptcy;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-201(1)(i): an assignee for the benefit of creditors;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-201(1)(j): a partner;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-201(1)(k): an agent;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-201(1)(l): an officer of a corporation, public or private;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-201(1)(m): a public officer; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-201(1)(nn): any other person acting in a fiduciary capacity for any person, trust, or estate.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-201(2): "Good faith" means something is in fact done honestly regardless of whether it is done negligently or not.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-201(3): "Principal" means a person to whom a fiduciary owes an obligation.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-202 Transactions prior to May 12, 1925.
-------------------------------------------------------------------
The provisions of this part do not apply to transactions taking place prior to May 12, 1925.

Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-203 Payments or transfers made to a fiduciary.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-203(1): A person who in good faith pays or transfers to a fiduciary any money or other property that the fiduciary is authorized to receive is not responsible for the proper application of the money or property by the fiduciary.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-203(2): A right or title acquired from the fiduciary in consideration of a payment or transfer described in Subsection (1) is not invalid as a consequence of a misapplication by the fiduciary.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-204 Transfer of negotiable instruments by a fiduciary.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-204(1): If a fiduciary endorses a negotiable instrument that is payable or endorsed to the fiduciary or the fiduciary's principal, and the fiduciary has authority to endorse the negotiable instrument on behalf of the principal, the person that receives the negotiable instrument through the endorsement:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-204(1)(a): is not bound to inquire as to whether the fiduciary is committing a breach of the fiduciary's obligation in endorsing or delivering the negotiable instrument; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-204(1)(b): is not required to provide notice that the fiduciary is committing a breach of the fiduciary's obligation, unless the person:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-204(1)(b)(i): takes the negotiable instrument with actual knowledge that the fiduciary is committing a breach of the fiduciary's obligation; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-204(1)(b)(ii): knows that taking the negotiable instrument amounts to bad faith.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-204(2): Notwithstanding Subsection (1), a person is liable to a principal if:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-204(2)(a): the fiduciary transfers a negotiable instrument to the person and the person knows that the fiduciary is transferring the negotiable instrument:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-204(2)(a)(i): as payment of, or as a security for, a personal debt of the fiduciary; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-204(2)(a)(ii): for the personal benefit of the fiduciary; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-204(2)(b): the fiduciary commits a breach of the fiduciary's obligation in transferring the negotiable instrument to the person.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-205 Checks -- Drawn by a fiduciary and payable to a third person.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-205(1): If a fiduciary draws a check or other bill of exchange in the name of the fiduciary's principal and the fiduciary has authority to draw the check or other bill of exchange in the name of the principal, the person to which the check or other bill of exchange is paid:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-205(1)(a): is not bound to inquire as to whether the fiduciary is committing a breach of the fiduciary's obligation in drawing the check or other bill of exchange; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-205(1)(b): is not required to provide notice that the fiduciary is committing a breach of the fiduciary's obligation, unless the person:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-205(1)(b)(i): takes the check or other bill of exchange with actual knowledge that the fiduciary is committing a breach of the fiduciary's obligation; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-205(1)(b)(ii): knows that taking the check or other bill of exchange amounts to bad faith.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-205(2): Notwithstanding Subsection (1), a person is liable to a principal if:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-205(2)(a): the fiduciary writes and delivers the check or other bill of exchange to the person;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-205(2)(b): the person knows that the fiduciary is drawing and delivering the check or other bill of exchange for:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-205(2)(b)(i): payment of, or as a security for, a personal debt of the fiduciary; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-205(2)(b)(ii): the personal benefit of the fiduciary; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-205(2)(c): the fiduciary commits a breach of the fiduciary's obligation in drawing or delivering the check or other bill of exchange to the person.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-206 Checks drawn by or payable to a fiduciary.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------
If a fiduciary draws a check or other bill of exchange in the name of the fiduciary's principal and the fiduciary has authority to draw the check or other bill of exchange that is payable to the fiduciary or a person that transfers the payment to the fiduciary, the person to which the check or other bill of exchange is paid:Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-206(1): is not bound to inquire as to whether the fiduciary is committing a breach of the fiduciary's obligation in transferring the check or other bill of exchange to the fiduciary; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-206(2): is not required to provide notice that the fiduciary is committing a breach of the fiduciary's obligation, unless the person:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-206(2)(a): takes the check or other bill of exchange with actual knowledge that the fiduciary is committing a breach of the fiduciary's obligation; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-206(2)(b): knows that taking the check or other bill of exchange amounts to bad faith.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-207 Bank deposits in the name of a fiduciary.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-207(1): If a fiduciary deposits a check in a bank in the name of the fiduciary's principal and to the credit of the fiduciary and the bank is authorized to pay the amount of the deposit or any part of the deposit, the bank is not liable to the principal unless:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-207(1)(a): the bank pays the check with actual knowledge that the fiduciary is committing a breach of the fiduciary's obligation in drawing the check; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-207(1)(b): the bank knows that paying the check amounts to bad faith.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-207(2): Notwithstanding Subsection (1), a bank is liable to a principal if:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-207(2)(a): the fiduciary deposits a check in the name of the principal as payment to the bank for payment of, or as security for, a personal debt of the fiduciary; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-207(2)(b): the fiduciary commits a breach of the fiduciary's obligation in drawing or delivering the check to the bank.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-208 Checks drawn in name of a principal.
--------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-208(1): If a fiduciary draws a check upon the account of the fiduciary's principal in a bank that is authorized to draw checks upon the principal's account and the bank is authorized to pay the check, the bank is not liable to the principal unless:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-208(1)(a): the bank pays the check with actual knowledge that the fiduciary is committing a breach of the fiduciary's obligation in drawing the check; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-208(1)(b): the bank knows that paying the check amounts to bad faith.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-208(2): Notwithstanding Subsection (1), the bank is liable to a principal if:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-208(2)(a): the principal's fiduciary deposits a check in the name of the principal as payment to the bank for payment of, or as security for, a personal debt of the fiduciary; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-208(2)(b): the fiduciary commits a breach of the fiduciary's obligation in drawing or delivering the check to the bank.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-209 Deposits in a fiduciary's personal account.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------
If a principal authorizes a fiduciary to write or endorse a check for the principal, and the fiduciary writes a check payable to the fiduciary and deposits the check in a bank into the fiduciary's personal account:Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-209(1): the bank is not bound to inquire whether a fiduciary is committing a breach of the fiduciary's obligation to a principal; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-209(2): the bank is authorized to pay the amount of the deposit or any part of a personal check of the fiduciary without being liable to the principal unless:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-209(2)(a): the bank deposits the check for a fiduciary with actual knowledge that the fiduciary is committing a breach of the fiduciary's obligation in depositing the check; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-209(2)(b): the bank knows that depositing the check for the fiduciary amounts to bad faith.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-210 Deposits in name of several trustees.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
When a deposit is made in a bank in the name of two or more persons as trustees and a check is drawn upon the trust account by a trustee authorized by another trustee to draw checks upon the trust account:Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-210(1): the payee or bank is not bound to inquire whether the deposit is a breach of trust to authorize a trustee to draw checks upon the trust account; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-1-210(2): the payee or bank is not liable unless the circumstances are such that the action of the payee or bank amounts to bad faith.


Utah Code Annotated - Title 75A - Chapter 2 - Uniform Power of Attorney Act
***************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-101 Reserved.
-----------------------------------------
Reserved.

Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-102 Definitions for chapter.
--------------------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-102(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-102(1)(a): "Agent" means a person granted authority to act for a principal under a power of attorney, whether denominated an agent, attorney-in-fact, or otherwise.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-102(1)(b): "Agent" includes an original agent, coagent, successor agent, and person to which an agent's authority is delegated.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-102(2): 75-1-201 "Beneficiary" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-102(3): 75-1-201 "Beneficiary designation" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-102(4): 75-1-201 "Child" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-102(5): 75-1-201 "Claims" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-102(6): 75-1-201 "Conservator" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-102(7): 75-1-201 "Descendant" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-102(8): "Durable," with respect to a power of attorney, means not terminated by the principal's incapacity.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-102(9): "Electronic" means relating to technology having electrical, digital, magnetic, wireless, optical, electromagnetic, or similar capabilities.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-102(10): 75-1-201 "Estate" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-102(11): 75-1-201 "Fiduciary" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-102(12): "Good faith" means honesty in fact.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-102(13): 75-1-201 "Guardian" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-102(14): "Incapacity" means the inability of an individual to manage property or business affairs because the individual:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-102(14)(a): has an impairment in the ability to receive and evaluate information or make or communicate decisions even with the use of technological assistance; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-102(14)(b): is:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-102(14)(b)(i): missing;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-102(14)(b)(ii): detained, including incarcerated in a penal system; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-102(14)(b)(iii): outside the United States and unable to return.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-102(15): 75-1-201 "Lease" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-102(16): 75-1-201 "Mortgage" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-102(17): 75-1-201 "Organization" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-102(18): "Person" means an individual, corporation, business trust, estate, trust, partnership, limited liability company, association, joint venture, public corporation, government or governmental subdivision, agency, or instrumentality, or any other legal or commercial entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-102(19): 75-1-201 "Personal representative" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-102(20): "Power of attorney" means a writing or other record that grants authority to an agent to act in the place of the principal, whether or not the term power of attorney is used.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-102(21): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-102(21)(a): "Presently exercisable general power of appointment," with respect to property or a property interest subject to a power of appointment, means power exercisable at the time in question to vest absolute ownership in the principal individually, the principal's estate, the principal's creditors, or the creditors of the principal's estate.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-102(21)(b): "Presently exercisable general power of appointment" includes a power of appointment not exercisable until the occurrence of a specified event, the satisfaction of an ascertainable standard, or the passage of a specified period only after the occurrence of the specified event, the satisfaction of the ascertainable standard, or the passage of the specified period.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-102(21)(c): "Presently exercisable general power of appointment" does not include a power exercisable in a fiduciary capacity or only by will.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-102(22): "Principal" means an individual who grants authority to an agent in a power of attorney.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-102(23): "Property" means anything that may be the subject of ownership, whether real or personal, or legal or equitable, or any interest or right therein.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-102(24): "Record" means information that is inscribed on a tangible medium or that is stored in an electronic or other medium and is retrievable in perceivable form.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-102(25): 75-1-201 "Security" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-102(26): "Sign" means, with present intent to authenticate or adopt a record:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-102(26)(a): to execute or adopt a tangible symbol; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-102(26)(b): to attach to or logically associate with the record an electronic sound, symbol, or process.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-102(27): "State" means a state of the United States, the District of Columbia, Puerto Rico, the United States Virgin Islands, or any territory or insular possession subject to the jurisdiction of the United States.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-102(28): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-102(28)(a): "Stocks and bonds" means stocks, bonds, mutual funds, and all other types of securities and financial instruments, whether held directly, indirectly, or in any other manner.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-102(28)(b): "Stocks and bonds" does not include commodity futures contracts and call or put options on stocks or stock indexes.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-102(29): 75-1-201 "Trust" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-102(30): 75-1-201 "Trustee" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-102(31): 75-1-201 "Will" means the same as that term is defined in Section


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-103 Applicability.
----------------------------------------------
This chapter applies to all powers of attorney except:Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-103(1): a power to the extent it is coupled with an interest in the subject of the power, including a power given to or for the benefit of a creditor in connection with a credit transaction;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-103(2): a power to make health care decisions;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-103(3): a proxy or other delegation to exercise voting rights or management rights with respect to an entity; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-103(4): a power created on a form prescribed by a government or governmental subdivision, agency, or instrumentality for a governmental purpose.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-104 Power of attorney is durable.
-------------------------------------------------------------
A power of attorney created under this chapter is durable unless it expressly provides that it is terminated by the incapacity of the principal.

Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-105 Execution of power of attorney.
---------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-105(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-105(1)(a): A power of attorney shall be signed by the principal or in the principal's conscious presence by another individual directed by the principal to sign the principal's name on the power of attorney before a notary public or other individual authorized by the law to take acknowledgments.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-105(1)(b): A signature on a power of attorney is presumed to be genuine if the principal acknowledges the signature before a notary public or other individual authorized by law to take acknowledgments.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-105(2): If the principal resides or is about to reside in a hospital, assisted living, skilled nursing, or similar facility, at the time of execution of the power of attorney, the principal may not name any agent that is the owner, operator, health care provider, or employee of the hospital, assisted living facility, skilled nursing, or similar residential care facility unless:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-105(2)(a): the agent is the spouse, legal guardian, or next of kin of the principal; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-105(2)(b): the agent's authority is strictly limited to the purpose of assisting the principal to establish eligibility for Medicaid.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-105(3): 76-5-111.4 A violation of Subsection (2) is a violation of Section


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-106 Validity of power of attorney.
--------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-106(1): 75A-2-105 A power of attorney executed in this state on or after May 10, 2016, is valid if its execution complies with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-106(2): A power of attorney executed in this state before May 10, 2016, is valid if its execution complied with the law of this state as it existed at the time of execution.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-106(3): 75A-2-107 A power of attorney executed other than in this state is valid in this state if, when the power of attorney was executed, the execution complied with:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-106(3)(a): 75A-2-107 the law of the jurisdiction that determines the meaning and effect of the power of attorney pursuant to Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-106(3)(b): the requirements for a military power of attorney pursuant to 10 U.S.C. Sec. 1044b.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-106(4): Except as otherwise provided by statute other than this chapter, a photocopy or electronically transmitted copy of an original power of attorney has the same effect as the original. For transactions involving real property, the copy of the power of attorney may be recorded in the county where the transaction lies when attached to an affidavit of the person accepting the power of attorney.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-107 Meaning and effect of power of attorney.
------------------------------------------------------------------------
The meaning and effect of a power of attorney is determined by the law of the jurisdiction indicated in the power of attorney and, in the absence of an indication of jurisdiction, by the law of the jurisdiction in which the power of attorney was executed.

Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-108 Nomination of conservator or guardian -- Adequacy of power of attorney -- Relation of agent to conservator or other fiduciary.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-108(1): 75-1-201 In a power of attorney, a principal may nominate a conservator of the principal's estate or a guardian of the principal's person for consideration by the court if protective proceedings, as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-108(2): If a principal executes a power of attorney and a petition is filed to appoint a conservator of the principal's estate, the court shall consider whether:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-108(2)(a): the provisions in the power of attorney are adequate to manage and protect the principal's estate without appointing a conservator; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-108(2)(b): the appointment of a conservator is necessary to manage and protect the principal's estate.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-108(3): If the court appoints a conservator of the principal's estate or a guardian of the principal's person, the court shall appoint a conservator or a guardian in accordance with the principal's most recent nomination unless there is good cause shown or disqualification.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-108(4): If, after a principal executes a power of attorney, the court determines that an appointment of a conservator or other fiduciary is necessary to manage and protect some or all of the principal's estate:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-108(4)(a): the agent named in the principal's power of attorney is accountable to the conservator or other fiduciary as well as the principal; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-108(4)(b): the power of attorney is not terminated and the agent's authority continues unless limited, suspended, or terminated by the court.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-109 When power of attorney is effective.
--------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-109(1): A power of attorney is effective when executed unless the principal provides in the power of attorney that it becomes effective at a future date or upon the occurrence of a future event or contingency.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-109(2): If a power of attorney becomes effective upon the occurrence of a future event or contingency, the principal, in the power of attorney, may authorize one or more persons to determine in a writing or other record that the event or contingency has occurred.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-109(3): 75A-2-102; 75A-2-102 If a power of attorney becomes effective upon the principal's incapacity and the principal has not authorized a person to determine whether the principal is incapacitated, or the person authorized is unable or unwilling to make the determination, the power of attorney becomes effective upon a determination in a writing or other record by:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-109(3)(a): 75A-2-102 a physician that the principal is incapacitated within the meaning of Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-109(3)(b): 75A-2-102 an attorney at law, a judge, or an appropriate governmental official that the principal is incapacitated within the meaning of Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-109(4): A person authorized by the principal in the power of attorney to determine that the principal is incapacitated may act as the principal's personal representative pursuant to the Health Insurance Portability and Accountability Act, Sections 1171 through 1179 of the Social Security Act, 42 U.S.C. Sec. 1320d, and applicable regulations, to obtain access to the principal's health care information and communicate with the principal's health care provider.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-110 Termination of power of attorney or agent's authority.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-110(1): A power of attorney terminates when:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-110(1)(a): the principal dies;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-110(1)(b): the principal becomes incapacitated, if the power of attorney is not durable;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-110(1)(c): the principal revokes the power of attorney;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-110(1)(d): the power of attorney provides that it terminates;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-110(1)(e): the purpose of the power of attorney is accomplished; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-110(1)(f): the principal revokes the agent's authority or the agent dies, becomes incapacitated, or resigns, and the power of attorney does not provide for another agent to act under the power of attorney.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-110(2): An agent's authority terminates when:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-110(2)(a): the principal revokes the authority;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-110(2)(b): the agent dies, becomes incapacitated, or resigns;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-110(2)(c): an action is filed for the dissolution or annulment of the agent's marriage to the principal or their legal separation, unless the power of attorney otherwise provides; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-110(2)(d): the power of attorney terminates.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-110(3): Unless the power of attorney otherwise provides, an agent's authority is exercisable until the authority terminates under Subsection (2), notwithstanding a lapse of time since the execution of the power of attorney.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-110(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-110(4)(a): Termination of an agent's authority or of a power of attorney is not effective as to the agent or another person that, without actual knowledge of the termination, acts in good faith under the power of attorney.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-110(4)(b): An act so performed, unless otherwise invalid or unenforceable, binds the principal and the principal's successors in interest.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-110(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-110(5)(a): Incapacity of the principal of a power of attorney that is not durable does not revoke or terminate the power of attorney as to an agent or other person that, without actual knowledge of the incapacity, acts in good faith under the power of attorney.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-110(5)(b): An act so performed, unless otherwise invalid or unenforceable, binds the principal and the principal's successors in interest.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-110(6): The execution of a power of attorney does not revoke a power of attorney previously executed by the principal unless the subsequent power of attorney provides that the previous power of attorney is revoked or that all other powers of attorney are revoked.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-110(7): The principal may revoke or amend a power of attorney:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-110(7)(a): by substantial compliance with a method provided in the terms of the power of attorney that expressly excludes all other methods for amending or revoking the power of attorney; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-110(7)(b): if the terms of the power of attorney do not provide a method or the method provided in the terms is not expressly made exclusive, by any other method manifesting clear and convincing evidence of the principal's intent.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-111 Coagents and successor agents.
--------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-111(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-111(1)(a): A principal may designate two or more persons to act as coagents.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-111(1)(b): Unless the power of attorney otherwise provides, each coagent may exercise its authority independently.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-111(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-111(2)(a): A principal may designate one or more successor agents to act if an agent resigns, dies, becomes incapacitated, is not qualified to serve, or declines to serve.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-111(2)(b): A principal may grant authority to designate one or more successor agents to an agent or other person designated by name, office, or function.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-111(2)(c): Unless the power of attorney otherwise provides, a successor agent:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-111(2)(c)(i): has the same authority as that granted to the original agent; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-111(2)(c)(ii): may not act until all predecessor agents have resigned, died, become incapacitated, are no longer qualified to serve, or have declined to serve.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-111(3): Except as otherwise provided in the power of attorney and Subsection (4), an agent that does not participate in or conceal a breach of fiduciary duty committed by another agent, including a predecessor agent, is not liable for the actions of the other agent.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-111(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-111(4)(a): An agent that has accepted appointment and that has actual knowledge of a breach or imminent breach of fiduciary duty by another agent shall notify the principal and, if the principal is incapacitated, take any action reasonably appropriate in the circumstances to safeguard the principal's best interest.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-111(4)(b): An agent that fails to notify the principal or take action as required by this subsection is liable for the reasonably foreseeable damages that could have been avoided if the agent had notified the principal or taken action.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-112 Reimbursement and compensation of agent.
------------------------------------------------------------------------
Unless the power of attorney otherwise provides, an agent is entitled to reimbursement of expenses reasonably incurred on behalf of the principal and to compensation that is reasonable under the circumstances.

Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-113 Agent's acceptance.
---------------------------------------------------
Except as otherwise provided in the power of attorney, a person accepts appointment as an agent under a power of attorney by exercising authority or performing duties as an agent or by any other assertion or conduct indicating acceptance.

Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-114 Agent's duties.
-----------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-114(1): Notwithstanding provisions in the power of attorney, an agent that has accepted appointment shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-114(1)(a): act in accordance with the principal's reasonable expectations to the extent actually known by the agent and, otherwise, in the principal's best interest;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-114(1)(b): act in good faith;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-114(1)(c): act only within the scope of authority granted in the power of attorney; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-114(1)(d): comply with the terms of the power of attorney.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-114(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-114(2)(a): Except as otherwise provided in the power of attorney or other provision of this chapter, an agent that has accepted appointment shall have no further obligation to act under the power of attorney.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-114(2)(b): However, with respect to any action taken by the agent under the power of attorney, the agent shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-114(2)(b)(i): act loyally for the principal's benefit;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-114(2)(b)(ii): act so as not to create a conflict of interest that impairs the agent's ability to act impartially in the principal's best interest;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-114(2)(b)(iii): act with the care, competence, and diligence ordinarily exercised by agents in similar circumstances;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-114(2)(b)(iv): keep a record of all receipts, disbursements, and transactions made on behalf of the principal;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-114(2)(b)(v): cooperate with a person that has authority to make health care decisions for the principal to carry out the principal's reasonable expectations to the extent actually known by the agent and, otherwise, act in the principal's best interest; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-114(2)(b)(vi): attempt to preserve the principal's estate plan, to the extent actually known by the agent, if preserving the plan is consistent with the principal's best interest based on all relevant factors, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-114(2)(b)(vi)(A): the value and nature of the principal's property;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-114(2)(b)(vi)(B): the principal's foreseeable obligations and need for maintenance;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-114(2)(b)(vi)(C): minimization of taxes, including income, estate, inheritance, generation-skipping transfer, and gift taxes; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-114(2)(b)(vi)(D): eligibility for a benefit, a program, or assistance under a statute, rule, or regulation.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-114(3): An agent that acts in good faith is not liable to any beneficiary of the principal's estate plan for failure to preserve the plan.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-114(4): An agent that acts with care, competence, and diligence for the best interest of the principal is not liable solely because the agent also benefits from the act or has an individual or conflicting interest in relation to the property or affairs of the principal.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-114(5): If an agent is selected by the principal because of special skills or expertise possessed by the agent or in reliance on the agent's representation that the agent has special skills or expertise, the special skills or expertise shall be considered in determining whether the agent has acted with care, competence, and diligence under the circumstances.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-114(6): Absent a breach of duty to the principal, an agent is not liable if the value of the principal's property declines.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-114(7): An agent that exercises authority to delegate to another person the authority granted by the principal or that engages another person on behalf of the principal is not liable for an act, error of judgment, or default of that person if the agent exercises care, competence, and diligence in selecting and monitoring the person.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-114(8): 75-1-201
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-114(8)(a): 75-1-201 Except as otherwise provided in the power of attorney, an agent is not required to disclose receipts, disbursements, or transactions conducted on behalf of the principal unless ordered by a court or requested by the principal, a guardian, a conservator, another fiduciary acting for the principal, a governmental agency having authority to protect the welfare of the principal, an interested person, as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-114(8)(b): If so requested, within 30 days the agent shall comply with the request or provide a writing or other record substantiating why additional time is needed and shall comply with the request within an additional 30 days.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-115 Exoneration of agent.
-----------------------------------------------------
A provision in a power of attorney relieving an agent of liability for breach of duty is binding on the principal and the principal's successors in interest except to the extent the provision:Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-115(1): relieves the agent of liability for breach of duty committed dishonestly, with an improper motive, or with reckless indifference to the purposes of the power of attorney or the best interest of the principal; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-115(2): was inserted as a result of an abuse of a confidential or fiduciary relationship with the principal.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-116 Judicial relief.
------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-116(1): 75-1-201 The following persons may petition a court to construe a power of attorney or review the agent's conduct and grant appropriate relief:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-116(1)(a): the principal or the agent;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-116(1)(b): a guardian, conservator, or other fiduciary acting for the principal;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-116(1)(c): a person authorized to make health care decisions for the principal;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-116(1)(d): 75-1-201 the principal's spouse, parent as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-116(1)(e): an individual who would qualify as a presumptive heir of the principal;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-116(1)(f): a person named as a beneficiary to receive any property, benefit, or contractual right on the principal's death or as a beneficiary of a trust created by or for the principal that has a financial interest in the principal's estate;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-116(1)(g): a governmental agency having regulatory authority to protect the welfare of the principal;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-116(1)(h): the principal's caregiver or another person that demonstrates sufficient interest in the principal's welfare; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-116(1)(i): a person asked to accept the power of attorney.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-116(2): Upon motion by the principal, the court shall dismiss a petition filed under this section, unless the court finds that the principal lacks capacity to revoke the agent's authority or the power of attorney.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-117 Agent's liability.
--------------------------------------------------
An agent that violates this chapter is liable to the principal or the principal's successors in interest for the amount required to:Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-117(1): restore the value of the principal's property to what it would have been had the violation not occurred; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-117(2): reimburse the principal or the principal's successors in interest for the attorney fees and costs paid on the agent's behalf.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-118 Agent's resignation -- Notice.
--------------------------------------------------------------
Unless the power of attorney provides a different method for an agent's resignation, an agent may resign by giving notice to the principal and, if the principal is incapacitated:Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-118(1): to the guardian, if one has been appointed for the principal, and a coagent or successor agent; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-118(2): if there is no person described in Subsection (1), to:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-118(2)(a): the principal's caregiver;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-118(2)(b): another person reasonably believed by the agent to have sufficient interest in the principal's welfare; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-118(2)(c): a governmental agency having authority to protect the welfare of the principal.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-119 Acceptance of and reliance upon acknowledged power of attorney.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-119(1): As used in this section, "acknowledged" means purportedly verified before a notary public or other individual authorized to take acknowledgements.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-119(2): 75A-2-105 A person that in good faith accepts an acknowledged power of attorney without actual knowledge that the signature is not genuine may rely upon the presumption under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-119(3): A person that in good faith accepts an acknowledged power of attorney without actual knowledge that the power of attorney is void, invalid, or terminated, that the purported agent's authority is void, invalid, or terminated, or that the agent is exceeding or improperly exercising the agent's authority may rely upon the power of attorney as if the power of attorney were genuine, valid, and still in effect, the agent's authority were genuine, valid, and still in effect, and the agent had not exceeded and had properly exercised the authority.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-119(4): A person that is asked to accept an acknowledged power of attorney may request, and rely upon, without further investigation:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-119(4)(a): an agent's certification under penalty of perjury of any factual matter concerning the principal, agent, or power of attorney;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-119(4)(b): an English translation of the power of attorney if the power of attorney contains, in whole or in part, language other than English; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-119(4)(c): an opinion of counsel as to any matter of law concerning the power of attorney if the person making the request provides in a writing or other record the reason for the request.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-119(5): An English translation or an opinion of counsel requested under this section shall be provided at the principal's expense unless the request is made more than seven business days after the power of attorney is presented for acceptance.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-119(6): 75A-2-120 For purposes of this section and Section


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-120 Liability for refusal to accept acknowledged power of attorney.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-120(1): 75A-2-119 As used in this section, "acknowledged" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-120(2): 75A-2-119; 75A-2-119 Except as otherwise provided in Subsection (3):
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-120(2)(a): 75A-2-119 a person shall either accept an acknowledged power of attorney or request a certification, a translation, or an opinion of counsel under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-120(2)(b): 75A-2-119 if a person requests a certification, a translation, or an opinion of counsel under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-120(2)(c): a person may not require an additional or different form of power of attorney for authority granted in the power of attorney presented.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-120(3): 75A-2-119; 75A-2-119 A person is not required to accept an acknowledged power of attorney if:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-120(3)(a): the person is not otherwise required to engage in a transaction with the principal in the same circumstances;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-120(3)(b): engaging in a transaction with the agent or the principal in the same circumstances would be inconsistent with federal law;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-120(3)(c): the person has actual knowledge of the termination of the agent's authority or of the power of attorney before exercise of the power;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-120(3)(d): 75A-2-119 a request for a certification, a translation, or an opinion of counsel under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-120(3)(e): 75A-2-119 the person in good faith believes that the power is not valid or that the agent does not have the authority to perform the act requested, whether or not a certification, a translation, or an opinion of counsel under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-120(3)(f): the person makes, or has actual knowledge that another person has made, a report to the Division of Aging and Adult Services stating a good faith belief that the principal may be subject to physical or financial abuse, neglect, exploitation, or abandonment by the agent or a person acting for or with the agent.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-120(4): A person that refuses in violation of this section to accept an acknowledged power of attorney is subject to:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-120(4)(a): a court order mandating acceptance of the power of attorney; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-120(4)(b): liability for reasonable attorney fees and costs incurred in any action or proceeding that confirms the validity of the power of attorney or mandates acceptance of the power of attorney.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-120(5): Court proceedings under this section shall be conducted pursuant to the terms in the Uniform Probate Code governing venue and procedures.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-121 Principles of law and equity.
-------------------------------------------------------------
Unless displaced by a provision of this chapter, the principles of law and equity supplement this act.

Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-122 Laws applicable to financial institutions and entities.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
This chapter does not supersede any other law applicable to financial institutions or other entities, and the other law controls if inconsistent with this chapter.

Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-123 Remedies under other law.
---------------------------------------------------------
The remedies under this chapter are not exclusive and do not abrogate any right or remedy under the law of this state other than this chapter.

Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-201 Authority that requires specific grant -- Grant of general authority.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-201(1): An agent under a power of attorney may do the following on behalf of the principal or with the principal's property only if the power of attorney expressly grants the agent the authority, and exercise of the authority is not otherwise prohibited by another agreement or instrument to which the authority or property is subject:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-201(1)(a): create, amend, revoke, or terminate an inter vivos trust;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-201(1)(b): make a gift;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-201(1)(c): create or change rights of survivorship;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-201(1)(d): create or change a beneficiary designation;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-201(1)(e): delegate authority granted under the power of attorney;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-201(1)(f): waive the principal's right to be a beneficiary of a joint and survivor annuity, including a survivor benefit under a retirement plan;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-201(1)(g): exercise fiduciary powers that the principal has authority to delegate; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-201(1)(h): disclaim property or otherwise exercise a power of appointment.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-201(2): Notwithstanding a grant of authority to do an act described in Subsection (1), unless the power of attorney otherwise provides, an agent that is not an ancestor, spouse, or descendant of the principal may not exercise authority under a power of attorney to create in the agent, or in an individual to whom the agent owes a legal obligation of support, an interest in the principal's property, whether by gift, right of survivorship, beneficiary designation, disclaimer, or otherwise.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-201(3): 75A-2-204; 75A-2-216 Subject to Subsections (1), (2), (4), and (5), if a power of attorney grants to an agent authority to do all acts that a principal could do, the agent has the general authority described in Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-201(4): 75A-2-217 Unless the power of attorney otherwise provides, a grant of authority to make a gift is subject to Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-201(5): Subject to Subsections (1), (2), and (4), if the subjects over which authority is granted in a power of attorney are similar or overlap, the broadest authority controls.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-201(6): Authority granted in a power of attorney is exercisable with respect to property that the principal has when the power of attorney is executed or acquires later, whether or not the property is located in this state and whether or not the authority is exercised or the power of attorney is executed in this state.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-201(7): An act performed by an agent pursuant to a power of attorney has the same effect, inures to the benefit of, and binds the principal and the principal's successors in interest as if the principal had performed the act.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-202 Incorporation of authority.
-----------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-202(1): 75A-2-204; 75A-2-217 An agent has authority described in this part if the power of attorney refers to general authority with respect to the descriptive term for the subjects stated in Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-202(2): 75A-2-204; 75A-2-217; 75A-2-204; 75A-2-217 A reference in a power of attorney to general authority with respect to the descriptive term for a subject in Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-202(3): A principal may modify authority incorporated by reference.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-203 Construction of authority generally.
--------------------------------------------------------------------
Except as otherwise provided in the power of attorney, by executing a power of attorney that incorporates by reference a subject described in SectionsUtah Code Annotated § 75A-2-203(1): demand, receive, and obtain, by litigation or otherwise, money or another thing of value to which the principal is, may become, or claims to be entitled, and conserve, invest, disburse, or use anything so received or obtained for the purposes intended;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-203(2): contract in any manner with any person, on terms agreeable to the agent, to accomplish a purpose of a transaction and perform, rescind, cancel, terminate, reform, restate, release, or modify the contract or another contract made by or on behalf of the principal;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-203(3): execute, acknowledge, seal, deliver, file, or record any instrument or communication the agent considers desirable to accomplish a purpose of a transaction, including creating at any time a schedule listing some or all of the principal's property and attaching it to the power of attorney;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-203(4): initiate, participate in, submit to alternative dispute resolution, settle, oppose, or propose or accept a compromise with respect to a claim existing in favor of or against the principal or intervene in litigation relating to the claim;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-203(5): seek on the principal's behalf the assistance of a court or other governmental agency to carry out an act authorized in the power of attorney;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-203(6): engage, compensate, and discharge an attorney, accountant, discretionary investment manager, expert witness, or other advisor;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-203(7): prepare, execute, and file a record, report, or other document to safeguard or promote the principal's interest under a statute or regulation;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-203(8): communicate with any representative or employee of a government or governmental subdivision, agency, or instrumentality on behalf of the principal;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-203(9): access communications intended for, and communicate on behalf of the principal, whether by mail, electronic transmission, telephone, or other means; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-203(10): do any lawful act with respect to the subject and all property related to the subject.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-204 Real property.
----------------------------------------------
Unless the power of attorney otherwise provides, language in a power of attorney granting general authority with respect to real property authorizes the agent to:Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-204(1): demand, buy, lease, receive, accept as a gift or as security for an extension of credit, or otherwise acquire or reject an interest in real property or a right incident to real property;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-204(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-204(2)(a): sell;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-204(2)(b): exchange;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-204(2)(c): convey with or without covenants, representations, or warranties;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-204(2)(d): quitclaim;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-204(2)(e): release;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-204(2)(f): surrender;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-204(2)(g): retain title for security;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-204(2)(h): encumber;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-204(2)(i): partition;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-204(2)(j): consent to partitioning;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-204(2)(k): subject to an easement or covenant;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-204(2)(l): subdivide;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-204(2)(m): apply for zoning or other governmental permits;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-204(2)(nn): plat or consent to platting;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-204(2)(oo): develop;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-204(2)(pp): grant an option concerning;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-204(2)(qq): lease;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-204(2)(rr): sublease;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-204(2)(ss): contribute to an entity in exchange for an interest in that entity; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-204(2)(tt): otherwise grant or dispose of an interest in real property or a right incident to real property;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-204(3): pledge or mortgage an interest in real property or right incident to real property as security to borrow money or pay, renew, or extend the time of payment of a debt of the principal or a debt guaranteed by the principal;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-204(4): release, assign, satisfy, or enforce by litigation or otherwise a mortgage, deed of trust, conditional sale contract, encumbrance, lien, or other claim to real property that exists or is asserted;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-204(5): manage or conserve an interest in real property or a right incident to real property owned or claimed to be owned by the principal, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-204(5)(a): insuring against liability or casualty or other loss;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-204(5)(b): obtaining or regaining possession of or protecting the interest or right by litigation or otherwise;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-204(5)(c): paying, assessing, compromising, or contesting taxes or assessments or applying for and receiving refunds in connection with taxes or assessments; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-204(5)(d): purchasing supplies, hiring assistance or labor, and making repairs or alterations to the real property;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-204(6): use, develop, alter, replace, remove, erect, or install structures or other improvements upon real property in or incident to which the principal has, or claims to have, an interest or right;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-204(7): participate in a reorganization with respect to real property or an entity that owns an interest in or right incident to real property and receive, hold, and act with respect to stocks and bonds or other property received in a plan of reorganization, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-204(7)(a): selling or otherwise disposing of stocks and bonds;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-204(7)(b): exercising or selling an option, right of conversion, or similar right with respect to stocks and bonds; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-204(7)(c): exercising any voting rights in person or by proxy;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-204(8): change the form of title of an interest in or right incident to real property; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-204(9): dedicate to public use, with or without consideration, easements or other real property in which the principal has, or claims to have, an interest.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-205 Tangible personal property.
-----------------------------------------------------------
Unless the power of attorney otherwise provides, language in a power of attorney granting general authority with respect to tangible personal property authorizes the agent to:Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-205(1): demand, buy, receive, accept as a gift or as security for an extension of credit, or otherwise acquire or reject ownership or possession of tangible personal property or an interest in tangible personal property;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-205(2): sell; exchange; convey with or without covenants, representations, or warranties; quitclaim; release; surrender; create a security interest in; grant options concerning; lease; sublease; or otherwise dispose of tangible personal property or an interest in tangible personal property;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-205(3): grant a security interest in tangible personal property or an interest in tangible personal property as security to borrow money or pay, renew, or extend the time of payment of a debt of the principal or a debt guaranteed by the principal;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-205(4): release, assign, satisfy, or enforce by litigation or otherwise, a security interest, lien, or other claim on behalf of the principal, with respect to tangible personal property or an interest in tangible personal property;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-205(5): manage or conserve tangible personal property or an interest in tangible personal property on behalf of the principal, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-205(5)(a): insuring against liability, casualty, or other loss;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-205(5)(b): obtaining or regaining possession of or protecting the property or interest, by litigation or otherwise;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-205(5)(c): paying, assessing, compromising, or contesting taxes or assessments or applying for and receiving refunds in connection with taxes or assessments;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-205(5)(d): moving the property from place to place;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-205(5)(e): storing the property for hire or on a gratuitous bailment; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-205(5)(f): using and making repairs, alterations, or improvements to the property; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-205(6): change the form of title of an interest in tangible personal property.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-206 Stocks and bonds.
-------------------------------------------------
Unless the power of attorney otherwise provides, language in a power of attorney granting general authority with respect to stocks and bonds authorizes the agent to:Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-206(1): buy, sell, and exchange stocks and bonds;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-206(2): establish, continue, modify, or terminate an account with respect to stocks and bonds;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-206(3): pledge stocks and bonds as security to borrow, pay, renew, or extend the time of payment of a debt of the principal;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-206(4): receive certificates and other evidences of ownership with respect to stocks and bonds; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-206(5): exercise voting rights with respect to stocks and bonds in person or by proxy, enter into voting trusts, and consent to limitations on the right to vote.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-207 Commodities and options.
--------------------------------------------------------
Unless the power of attorney otherwise provides, language in a power of attorney granting general authority with respect to commodities and options authorizes the agent to:Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-207(1): buy, sell, exchange, assign, settle, and exercise commodity futures contracts and call or put options on stocks or stock indexes traded on a regulated option exchange; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-207(2): establish, continue, modify, and terminate option accounts.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-208 Banks and other financial institutions.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------
Unless the power of attorney otherwise provides, language in a power of attorney granting general authority with respect to banks and other financial institutions authorizes the agent to:Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-208(1): continue, modify, and terminate an account or other banking arrangement made by or on behalf of the principal;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-208(2): establish, modify, and terminate an account or other banking arrangement with a bank, trust company, savings and loan association, credit union, thrift company, brokerage firm, or other financial institution selected by the agent;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-208(3): contract for services available from a financial institution, including renting or closing a safe deposit box or space in a vault;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-208(4): withdraw, by check, order, electronic funds transfer, or otherwise, money or property of the principal deposited with or left in the custody of a financial institution;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-208(5): receive statements of account, vouchers, notices, and similar documents from a financial institution and act with respect to them;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-208(6): enter a safe deposit box or vault and withdraw or add to the contents;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-208(7): borrow money and pledge as security personal property of the principal necessary to borrow money or pay, renew, or extend the time of payment of a debt of the principal or a debt guaranteed by the principal;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-208(8): make, assign, draw, endorse, discount, guarantee, and negotiate promissory notes, checks, drafts, and other negotiable or nonnegotiable paper of the principal or payable to the principal or the principal's order, transfer money, receive the cash or other proceeds of those transactions, and accept a draft drawn by a person upon the principal and pay it when due;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-208(9): receive for the principal and act upon a sight draft, warehouse receipt, or other document of title whether tangible or electronic, or other negotiable or nonnegotiable instrument;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-208(10): apply for, receive, and use letters of credit, credit and debit cards, electronic transaction authorizations, and traveler's checks from a financial institution and give an indemnity or other agreement in connection with letters of credit; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-208(11): consent to an extension of the time of payment with respect to commercial paper or a financial transaction with a financial institution.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-209 Operation of entity or business.
----------------------------------------------------------------
Subject to the terms of a document or an agreement governing an entity or an entity ownership interest, and unless the power of attorney otherwise provides, language in a power of attorney granting general authority with respect to operation of an entity or business authorizes the agent to:Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-209(1): operate, buy, sell, enlarge, reduce, or terminate an ownership interest;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-209(2): perform a duty or discharge a liability and exercise in person or by proxy a right, power, privilege, or option that the principal has, may have, or claims to have;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-209(3): enforce the terms of an ownership agreement;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-209(4): initiate, participate in, submit to alternative dispute resolution, settle, oppose, or propose or accept a compromise with respect to litigation to which the principal is a party because of an ownership interest;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-209(5): exercise in person or by proxy, or enforce by litigation or otherwise, a right, power, privilege, or option the principal has or claims to have as the holder of stocks and bonds;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-209(6): initiate, participate in, submit to alternative dispute resolution, settle, oppose, or propose or accept a compromise with respect to litigation to which the principal is a party concerning stocks and bonds;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-209(7): with respect to an entity or business owned solely by the principal:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-209(7)(a): continue, modify, renegotiate, extend, and terminate a contract made by or on behalf of the principal with respect to the entity or business before execution of the power of attorney;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-209(7)(b): determine:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-209(7)(b)(i): the location of its operation;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-209(7)(b)(ii): the nature and extent of its business;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-209(7)(b)(iii): the methods of manufacturing, selling, merchandising, financing, accounting, and advertising employed in its operation;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-209(7)(b)(iv): the amount and types of insurance carried; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-209(7)(b)(v): the mode of engaging, compensating, and dealing with its employees and accountants, attorneys, or other advisors;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-209(7)(c): change the name or form of organization under which the entity or business is operated and enter into an ownership agreement with other persons to take over all or part of the operation of the entity or business; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-209(7)(d): demand and receive money due or claimed by the principal or on the principal's behalf in the operation of the entity or business and control and disburse the money in the operation of the entity or business;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-209(8): put additional capital into an entity or business in which the principal has an interest;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-209(9): join in a plan of reorganization, consolidation, conversion, domestication, or merger of the entity or business;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-209(10): sell or liquidate all or part of an entity or business;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-209(11): establish the value of an entity or business under a buy-out agreement to which the principal is a party;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-209(12): prepare, sign, file, and deliver reports, compilations of information, returns, or other papers with respect to an entity or business and make related payments; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-209(13): pay, compromise, or contest taxes, assessments, fines, or penalties and perform any other act to protect the principal from illegal or unnecessary taxation, assessments, fines, or penalties, with respect to an entity or business, including attempts to recover, in any manner permitted by law, money paid before or after the execution of the power of attorney.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-210 Insurance and annuities.
--------------------------------------------------------
Unless the power of attorney otherwise provides, language in a power of attorney granting general authority with respect to insurance and annuities authorizes the agent to:Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-210(1): continue, pay the premium or make a contribution on, modify, exchange, rescind, release, or terminate a contract procured by or on behalf of the principal that insures or provides an annuity to either the principal or another person, whether or not the principal is a beneficiary under the contract;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-210(2): procure new, different, and additional contracts of insurance and annuities for the principal and the principal's spouse, child, and other dependents, and select the amount, type of insurance or annuity, and mode of payment;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-210(3): pay the premium or make a contribution on, modify, exchange, rescind, release, or terminate a contract of insurance or annuity procured by the agent;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-210(4): apply for and receive a loan secured by a contract of insurance or annuity;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-210(5): surrender and receive the cash surrender value on a contract of insurance or annuity;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-210(6): exercise an election;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-210(7): exercise investment powers available under a contract of insurance or annuity;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-210(8): change the manner of paying premiums on a contract of insurance or annuity;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-210(9): change or convert the type of insurance or annuity with respect to which the principal has or claims to have authority described in this section;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-210(10): apply for and procure a benefit or assistance under a statute or regulation to guarantee or pay premiums of a contract of insurance on the life of the principal;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-210(11): collect, sell, assign, hypothecate, borrow against, or pledge the interest of the principal in a contract of insurance or annuity;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-210(12): select the form and timing of the payment of proceeds from a contract of insurance or annuity; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-210(13): pay, from proceeds or otherwise, compromise or contest, and apply for refunds in connection with a tax or assessment levied by a taxing authority with respect to a contract of insurance or annuity or its proceeds or liability accruing by reason of the tax or assessment.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-211 Estates, trusts, and other beneficial interests.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-211(1): As used in this section, "estate, trust, or other beneficial interest" means a trust, probate estate, guardianship, conservatorship, escrow, custodianship, or fund from which the principal is, may become, or claims to be entitled to a share or payment.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-211(2): Unless the power of attorney otherwise provides, language in a power of attorney granting general authority with respect to estates, trusts, and other beneficial interests authorizes the agent to:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-211(2)(a): accept, receive, receipt for, sell, assign, pledge, or exchange a share in or payment from an estate, trust, or other beneficial interest;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-211(2)(b): demand or obtain money or another thing of value to which the principal is, may become, or claims to be entitled by reason of an estate, trust, or other beneficial interest, by litigation or otherwise;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-211(2)(c): exercise for the benefit of the principal a presently exercisable general power of appointment held by the principal;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-211(2)(d): initiate, participate in, submit to alternative dispute resolution, settle, oppose, or propose or accept a compromise with respect to litigation to ascertain the meaning, validity, or effect of a deed, will, declaration of trust, or other instrument or transaction affecting the interest of the principal;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-211(2)(e): initiate, participate in, submit to alternative dispute resolution, settle, oppose, or propose or accept a compromise with respect to litigation to remove, substitute, or surcharge a fiduciary;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-211(2)(f): conserve, invest, disburse, or use anything received for an authorized purpose;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-211(2)(g): transfer an interest of the principal in real property, stocks and bonds, accounts with financial institutions or securities intermediaries, insurance, annuities, and other property to the trustee of a revocable trust created by the principal as settlor; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-211(2)(h): reject, renounce, disclaim, release, or consent to a reduction in or modification of a share in or payment from an estate, trust, or other beneficial interest.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-212 Claims and litigation.
------------------------------------------------------
Unless the power of attorney otherwise provides, language in a power of attorney granting general authority with respect to claims and litigation authorizes the agent to:Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-212(1): assert and maintain before a court or administrative agency a claim, claim for relief, cause of action, counterclaim, offset, recoupment, or defense, including an action to recover property or other thing of value, recover damages sustained by the principal, eliminate or modify tax liability, or seek an injunction, specific performance, or other relief;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-212(2): bring an action to determine adverse claims or intervene or otherwise participate in litigation;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-212(3): seek an attachment, garnishment, order of arrest, or other preliminary, provisional, or intermediate relief and use an available procedure to effect or satisfy a judgment, order, or decree;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-212(4): make or accept a tender, offer of judgment, or admission of facts, submit a controversy on an agreed statement of facts, consent to examination, and bind the principal in litigation;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-212(5): submit to alternative dispute resolution, settle, and propose or accept a compromise;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-212(6): waive the issuance and service of process upon the principal, accept service of process, appear for the principal, designate persons upon which process directed to the principal may be served, execute and file or deliver stipulations on the principal's behalf, verify pleadings, seek appellate review, procure and give surety and indemnity bonds, contract and pay for the preparation and printing of records and briefs, receive, execute, and file or deliver a consent, waiver, release, confession of judgment, satisfaction of judgment, notice, agreement, or other instrument in connection with the prosecution, settlement, or defense of a claim or litigation;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-212(7): act for the principal with respect to bankruptcy or insolvency, whether voluntary or involuntary, concerning the principal or some other person, or with respect to a reorganization, receivership, or application for the appointment of a receiver or trustee that affects an interest of the principal in property or other thing of value;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-212(8): pay a judgment, award, or order against the principal or a settlement made in connection with a claim or litigation; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-212(9): receive money or other thing of value paid in settlement of or as proceeds of a claim or litigation.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-213 Personal and family maintenance.
----------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-213(1): Unless the power of attorney otherwise provides, language in a power of attorney granting general authority with respect to personal and family maintenance authorizes the agent to:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-213(1)(a): perform the acts necessary to maintain the customary standard of living of the principal, the principal's spouse, and the following individuals, whether living when the power of attorney is executed or later born:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-213(1)(a)(i): a child of the principal;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-213(1)(a)(ii): other individuals legally entitled to be supported by the principal; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-213(1)(a)(iii): the individuals whom the principal has customarily supported or indicated the intent to support;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-213(1)(b): make periodic payments of child support and other family maintenance required by a court or governmental agency or an agreement to which the principal is a party;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-213(1)(c): provide living quarters for the individuals described in Subsection (1)(a) by:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-213(1)(c)(i): purchase, lease, or other contract; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-213(1)(c)(ii): paying the operating costs, including interest, amortization payments, repairs, improvements, and taxes, for premises owned by the principal or occupied by those individuals;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-213(1)(d): provide normal domestic help, usual vacations and travel expenses, and funds for shelter, clothing, food, appropriate education, including postsecondary and vocational education, and other current living costs for the individuals described in Subsection (1)(a);
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-213(1)(e): pay expenses for necessary health care and custodial care on behalf of the individuals described in Subsection (1)(a);
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-213(1)(f): act as the principal's personal representative pursuant to the Health Insurance Portability and Accountability Act, Sections 1171 through 1179 of the Social Security Act, 42 U.S.C. Sec. 1320d, and applicable regulations, in making decisions related to the past, present, or future payment for the provision of health care consented to by the principal or anyone authorized under the law of this state to consent to health care on behalf of the principal;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-213(1)(g): continue any provision made by the principal for automobiles or other means of transportation, including registering, licensing, insuring, and replacing them, for the individuals described in Subsection (1)(a);
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-213(1)(h): maintain credit and debit accounts and open new accounts for the convenience of the individuals described in Subsection (1)(a); and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-213(1)(i): continue payments incidental to the membership or affiliation of the principal in a religious institution, club, society, order, or other organization or to continue contributions to those organizations.
