Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-213(2): Authority with respect to personal and family maintenance is neither dependent upon, nor limited by, authority that an agent may or may not have with respect to gifts under this chapter.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-214 Benefits from governmental programs or civil or military service.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-214(1): As used in this section, "benefits from governmental programs or civil or military service" means any benefit, program, or assistance provided under a statute or regulation, including social security, Medicare, and Medicaid.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-214(2): 75A-2-213 Unless the power of attorney otherwise provides, language in a power of attorney granting general authority with respect to benefits from governmental programs or civil or military service authorizes the agent to:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-214(2)(a): 75A-2-213 execute vouchers in the name of the principal for allowances and reimbursements payable by the United States or a foreign government or by a state or subdivision of a state to the principal, including allowances and reimbursements for transportation of the individuals described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-214(2)(b): take possession and order the removal and shipment of property of the principal from a post, warehouse, depot, dock, or other place of storage or safekeeping, either governmental or private, and execute and deliver a release, voucher, receipt, bill of lading, shipping ticket, certificate, or other instrument for that purpose;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-214(2)(c): enroll in, apply for, select, reject, change, amend, or discontinue, on the principal's behalf, a benefit or program;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-214(2)(d): prepare, file, and maintain a claim of the principal for a benefit or assistance, financial or otherwise, to which the principal may be entitled under a statute or regulation;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-214(2)(e): initiate, participate in, submit to alternative dispute resolution, settle, oppose, or propose or accept a compromise with respect to litigation concerning any benefit or assistance the principal may be entitled to receive under a statute or regulation; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-214(2)(f): receive the financial proceeds of a claim described in Subsection (2)(d) and conserve, invest, disburse, or use for a lawful purpose anything received.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-215 Retirement plans.
-------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-215(1): As used in this section, "retirement plan" means a plan or account created by an employer, the principal, or another individual to provide retirement benefits or deferred compensation of which the principal is a participant, beneficiary, or owner, including a plan or account under the following sections of the Internal Revenue Code:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-215(1)(a): an individual retirement account under Section 408, Internal Revenue Code;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-215(1)(b): a Roth individual retirement account under Section 408A, Internal Revenue Code;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-215(1)(c): a deemed individual retirement account under Section 408(q), Internal Revenue Code;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-215(1)(d): an annuity or mutual fund custodial account under Section 403(b), Internal Revenue Code;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-215(1)(e): a pension, profit-sharing, stock bonus, or other retirement plan qualified under Section 401(a), Internal Revenue Code;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-215(1)(f): a plan under Section 457(b), Internal Revenue Code; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-215(1)(g): a nonqualified deferred compensation plan under Section 409A, Internal Revenue Code.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-215(2): Unless the power of attorney otherwise provides, language in a power of attorney granting general authority with respect to retirement plans authorizes the agent to:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-215(2)(a): select the form and timing of payments under a retirement plan and withdraw benefits from a plan;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-215(2)(b): make a rollover, including a direct trustee-to-trustee rollover, of benefits from one retirement plan to another;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-215(2)(c): establish a retirement plan in the principal's name;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-215(2)(d): make contributions to a retirement plan;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-215(2)(e): exercise investment powers available under a retirement plan; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-215(2)(f): borrow from, sell assets to, or purchase assets from a retirement plan.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-216 Taxes.
--------------------------------------
Unless the power of attorney otherwise provides, language in a power of attorney granting general authority with respect to taxes authorizes the agent to:Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-216(1): prepare, sign, and file federal, state, local, and foreign income, gift, payroll, property, Federal Insurance Contributions Act, and other tax returns, claims for refunds, requests for extension of time, petitions regarding tax matters, and any other tax-related documents, including receipts, offers, waivers, consents, including consents and agreements under Section 2032A, Internal Revenue Code, closing agreements, and any power of attorney required by the Internal Revenue Service or other taxing authority with respect to a tax year upon which the statute of limitations has not run and the following 25 tax years;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-216(2): pay taxes due, collect refunds, post bonds, receive confidential information, and contest deficiencies determined by the Internal Revenue Service or other taxing authority;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-216(3): exercise any election available to the principal under federal, state, local, or foreign tax law; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-216(4): act for the principal in all tax matters for all periods before the Internal Revenue Service or other taxing authority.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-217 Gifts.
--------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-217(1): Chapter 8, Uniform Transfers to Minors Act As used in this section, "for the benefit of" includes a gift to a trust, an account under
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-217(2): Unless the power of attorney otherwise provides, language in a power of attorney granting general authority with respect to gifts authorizes the agent only to:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-217(2)(a): make outright to, or for the benefit of, a person a gift of any of the principal's property, including by the exercise of a presently exercisable general power of appointment held by the principal, in an amount per donee not to exceed the annual dollar limits of the federal gift tax exclusion under Section 2503(b), Internal Revenue Code, without regard to whether the federal gift tax exclusion applies to the gift, or if the principal's spouse agrees to consent to a split gift pursuant to Section 2513, Internal Revenue Code, in an amount per donee not to exceed twice the annual federal gift tax exclusion limit; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-217(2)(b): consent, pursuant to Section 2513, Internal Revenue Code, to the splitting of a gift made by the principal's spouse in an amount per donee not to exceed the aggregate annual gift tax exclusions for both spouses.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-217(3): An agent may make a gift of the principal's property only as the agent determines is consistent with the principal's objectives if actually known by the agent and, if unknown, as the agent determines is consistent with the principal's best interest based on all relevant factors, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-217(3)(a): the value and nature of the principal's property;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-217(3)(b): the principal's foreseeable obligations and need for maintenance;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-217(3)(c): minimization of taxes, including income, estate, inheritance, generation-skipping transfer, and gift taxes;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-217(3)(d): eligibility for a benefit, program, or assistance under a statute or regulation; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-217(3)(e): the principal's personal history of making or joining in making gifts.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-301 Statutory form power of attorney.
-----------------------------------------------------------------
A document substantially in the following form may be used to create a statutory form power of attorney that has the meaning and effect prescribed by this chapter.

Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-302 Agent's certification.
------------------------------------------------------
The following optional form may be used by an agent to certify facts concerning a power of attorney.Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-302(1): the principal is alive and has not revoked the power of attorney or my authority to act under the power of attorney and the power of attorney and my authority to act under the power of attorney have not terminated;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-302(2): if the power of attorney was drafted to become effective upon the happening of an event or contingency, the event or contingency has occurred;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-302(3): if I was named as a successor agent, the prior agent is no longer able or willing to serve; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-302(4): _____________________________________________________________________ ______________________________________________________________________________ ______________________________________________________________________________ _______________________________________________________________________


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-401 Uniformity of application and construction.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------
In applying and construing this uniform act, consideration shall be given to the need to promote uniformity of the law with respect to its subject matter among the states that enact this uniform act.

Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-402 Relation to Electronic Signatures in Global and National Commerce Act.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
This chapter modifies, limits, and supersedes the federal Electronic Signatures in Global and National Commerce Act, 15 U.S.C. Sec. 7001 et seq., but does not modify, limit, or supersede Section 101(c) of that act, 15 U.S.C. Sec. 7001(c), or authorize electronic delivery of any of the notices described in Section 103(b) of that act, 15 U.S.C.  Sec. 7003(b).

Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-403 Effect on existing powers of attorney.
----------------------------------------------------------------------
Except as otherwise provided:Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-403(1): this chapter applies to a power of attorney created before, on, or after May 10, 2016;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-403(2): this chapter applies to a judicial proceeding concerning a power of attorney commenced on or after May 10, 2016;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-403(3): this chapter applies to a judicial proceeding concerning a power of attorney commenced before May 10, 2016, unless the court finds that application of a provision of this chapter would substantially interfere with the effective conduct of the judicial proceeding or prejudice the rights of a party, in which case that provision does not apply and the superseded law applies; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-2-403(4): an act done before May 10, 2016, is not affected by this chapter.


Utah Code Annotated - Title 75A - Chapter 3 - Health Care Decisions
*******************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101 Definitions for chapter.
--------------------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(1): "Adult" means an individual who is:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(1)(a): at least 18 years old; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(1)(b): an emancipated minor.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(2): "Advance health care directive":
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(2)(a): includes:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(2)(a)(i): a designation of an agent to make health care decisions for an adult when the adult cannot make or communicate health care decisions; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(2)(a)(ii): an expression of preferences about health care decisions;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(2)(b): may take one of the following forms:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(2)(b)(i): a written document, voluntarily executed by an adult in accordance with the requirements of this chapter; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(2)(b)(ii): a witnessed oral statement, made in accordance with the requirements of this chapter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(2)(c): does not include an order for life sustaining treatment.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(3): "Agent" means an adult designated in an advance health care directive to make health care decisions for the declarant.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(4): 58-31b-301 "APRN" means an individual who is:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(4)(a): 58-31b-301 certified or licensed as an advance practice registered nurse under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(4)(b): an independent practitioner; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(4)(c): acting within the scope of practice for that individual, as provided by law, rule, and specialized certification and training in that individual's area of practice.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(5): "Best interest" means that the benefits to the individual resulting from a treatment outweigh the burdens to the individual resulting from the treatment, taking into account:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(5)(a): the effect of the treatment on the physical, emotional, and cognitive functions of the individual;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(5)(b): the degree of physical pain or discomfort caused to the individual by the treatment or the withholding or withdrawal of treatment;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(5)(c): the degree to which the individual's medical condition, the treatment, or the withholding or withdrawal of treatment, result in a severe and continuing impairment of the dignity of the individual by subjecting the individual to humiliation and dependency;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(5)(d): the effect of the treatment on the life expectancy of the individual;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(5)(e): the prognosis of the individual for recovery with and without the treatment;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(5)(f): the risks, side effects, and benefits of the treatment, or the withholding or withdrawal of treatment; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(5)(g): the religious beliefs and basic values of the individual receiving treatment, to the extent these may assist the decision maker in determining the best interest.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(6): "Capacity to appoint an agent" means that the adult understands the consequences of appointing a particular individual as agent.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(7): 75-1-201 "Child" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(8): "Declarant" means an adult who has completed and signed or directed the signing of an advance health care directive.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(9): "Default surrogate" means the adult who may make decisions for an individual when either:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(9)(a): an agent or guardian has not been appointed; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(9)(b): an agent is not able, available, or willing to make decisions for an adult.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(10): "Emergency medical services provider" means a person that is licensed, designated, or certified under Title 53, Chapter 2d, Emergency Medical Services Act.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(11): 75-1-201 "Estate" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(12): 75A-3-303 "Generally accepted health care standards":
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(12)(a): 75A-3-303 is defined only for the purpose of:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(12)(a)(i): this chapter and does not define the standard of care for any other purpose under Utah law; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(12)(a)(ii): 75A-3-303 enabling health care providers to interpret the statutory form set forth in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(12)(b): means the standard of care that justifies a provider in declining to provide life sustaining care because the proposed life sustaining care:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(12)(b)(i): will not prevent or reduce the deterioration in the health or functional status of an individual;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(12)(b)(ii): will not prevent the impending death of an individual; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(12)(b)(iii): will impose more burden on the individual than any expected benefit to the individual.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(13): 75-1-201 "Guardian" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(14): "Health care" means any care, treatment, service, or procedure to improve, maintain, diagnose, or otherwise affect an individual's physical or mental condition.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(15): "Health care decision":
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(15)(a): means a decision about an adult's health care made by, or on behalf of, an adult, that is communicated to a health care provider;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(15)(b): includes:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(15)(b)(i): selection and discharge of a health care provider and a health care facility;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(15)(b)(ii): approval or disapproval of diagnostic tests, procedures, programs of medication, and orders not to resuscitate; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(15)(b)(iii): directions to provide, withhold, or withdraw artificial nutrition and hydration and all other forms of health care; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(15)(c): does not include decisions about an adult's financial affairs or social interactions other than as indirectly affected by the health care decision.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(16): "Health care decision making capacity" means an adult's ability to make an informed decision about receiving or refusing health care, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(16)(a): the ability to understand the nature, extent, or probable consequences of health status and health care alternatives;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(16)(b): the ability to make a rational evaluation of the burdens, risks, benefits, and alternatives of accepting or rejecting health care; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(16)(c): the ability to communicate a decision.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(17): "Health care facility" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(17)(a): a health care facility as defined in Title 26B, Chapter 2, Part 2, Health Care Facility Licensing and Inspection; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(17)(b): private offices of physicians, dentists, and other health care providers licensed to provide health care under Title 58, Occupations and Professions.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(18): 78B-3-403 "Health care provider" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(19): "Incapacitated" means the same as that term is defined in Section 75-1-201.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(20): 75-1-201 "Incapacity" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(21): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(21)(a): "Life sustaining care" means any medical intervention, including procedures, administration of medication, or use of a medical device, that maintains life by sustaining, restoring, or supplanting a vital function.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(21)(b): "Life sustaining care" does not include care provided for the purpose of keeping an individual comfortable.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(22): "Minor" means an individual who:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(22)(a): is under 18 years old; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(22)(b): is not an emancipated minor.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(23): 75-3-106 "Order for life sustaining treatment" means an order related to life sustaining treatment, on a form designated by the Department of Health and Human Services under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(24): 75-1-201 "Parent" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(25): 75-1-201 "Personal representative" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(26): "Physician" means a physician and surgeon or osteopathic surgeon licensed under Title 58, Chapter 67, Utah Medical Practice Act or Chapter 68, Utah Osteopathic Medical Practice Act.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(27): "Physician assistant" means an individual licensed as a physician assistant under Title 58, Chapter 70a, Utah Physician Assistant Act.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(28): "Reasonably available" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(28)(a): readily able to be contacted without undue effort; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(28)(b): willing and able to act in a timely manner considering the urgency of the circumstances.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(29): 75-1-201 "State" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(30): "Substituted judgment" means the standard to be applied by a surrogate when making a health care decision for an adult who previously had the capacity to make health care decisions, which requires the surrogate to consider:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(30)(a): specific preferences expressed by the adult:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(30)(a)(i): when the adult had the capacity to make health care decisions; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(30)(a)(ii): at the time the decision is being made;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(30)(b): the surrogate's understanding of the adult's health care preferences;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(30)(c): the surrogate's understanding of what the adult would have wanted under the circumstances; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(30)(d): to the extent that the preferences described in Subsections (30)(a) through (c) are unknown, the best interest of the adult.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(31): 75A-3-203 "Surrogate" means a health care decision maker who is:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(31)(a): an appointed agent;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(31)(b): 75A-3-203 a default surrogate under the provisions of Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(31)(c): a guardian.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(32): 75-1-201 "Trust" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-101(33): 75-1-201 "Will" means the same as that term is defined in Section


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-102 Intent statement.
-------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-102(1): The Legislature finds:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-102(1)(a): developments in health care technology make possible many alternatives for treating medical conditions and make possible the unnatural prolongation of life;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-102(1)(b): an adult should have the clear legal choice to:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-102(1)(b)(i): accept or reject health care, even if rejecting health care will result in death sooner than death would be expected to occur if rejected health care were started or continued;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-102(1)(b)(ii): be spared unwanted procedures; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-102(1)(b)(iii): be permitted to die with a maximum of dignity and function and a minimum of pain;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-102(1)(c): Utah law should:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-102(1)(c)(i): provide an adult with a legal tool to designate a health care agent and express preferences about health care options to go into effect only after the adult loses the ability to make or communicate health care decisions, including decisions about end-of-life care; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-102(1)(c)(ii): promote an advance health care directive system that can be administered effectively within the health care system;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-102(1)(d): surrogate decisions made on behalf of an adult who previously had capacity to make health care decisions, but who has lost health care decision making capacity should be based on:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-102(1)(d)(i): input from the incapacitated adult, to the extent possible under the circumstances;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-102(1)(d)(ii): specific preferences expressed by the adult prior to the loss of health care decision making capacity;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-102(1)(d)(iii): the surrogate's understanding of the adult's health care preferences; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-102(1)(d)(iv): the surrogate's understanding of what the adult would have wanted under the circumstances; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-102(1)(e): surrogate decisions made on behalf of an adult who has never had health care decision making capacity should be made on the basis of the adult's best interest.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-102(2): In recognition of the dignity and privacy that each adult is entitled to expect, and to protect the right of an adult to refuse to be treated without the adult's consent, the Legislature declares that this state recognizes the right to make binding advance health care directives directing health care providers to:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-102(2)(a): provide life sustaining medically indicated health care;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-102(2)(b): withhold or withdraw health care; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-102(2)(c): provide health care only to the extent set forth in an advance health care directive.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-103 Effect of chapter.
--------------------------------------------------
This chapter does not:Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-103(1): create a presumption concerning the intention of an adult who has not made or who has revoked an advance health care directive;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-103(2): authorize mercy killing, assisted suicide, or euthanasia; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-103(3): authorize the provision, withholding, or withdrawal of health care, to the extent prohibited by the laws of this state.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-104 Provisions cumulative with existing law.
------------------------------------------------------------------------
The provisions of this chapter are cumulative with existing law regarding a person's right to consent or refuse to consent to medical treatment and do not impair any existing rights or responsibilities that a health care provider, a person, including a minor or incapacitated person, or a person's family or surrogate may have in regard to the provision, withholding or withdrawal of life sustaining procedures under the common law or statutes of the state.

Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-105 Severability.
---------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-105(1): If any one or more provision, section, subsection, sentence, clause, phrase, or word of this chapter, or the application of this chapter to any person or circumstance, is found to be unconstitutional, the same is hereby declared to be severable and the balance of this chapter shall remain effective notwithstanding such unconstitutionality.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-105(2): The Legislature hereby declares that it would have passed this chapter, and each provision, section, subsection, sentence, clause, phrase, or word of this chapter, irrespective of the fact that any one or more provision, section, subsection, sentence, clause, phrase, or word be declared unconstitutional.


Utah Code Annotated § 75a-3-106 Emergency medical services -- Order for life sustaining treatment.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75a-3-106(1): An order for life sustaining treatment may be created by or on behalf of an individual as described in this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 75a-3-106(2): An order for life sustaining treatment shall, in consultation with the individual authorized to consent to the order pursuant to this section, be prepared by:
Utah Code Annotated § 75a-3-106(2)(a): the physician, APRN, or physician assistant of the individual to whom the order for life sustaining treatment relates; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75a-3-106(2)(b): a health care provider who:
Utah Code Annotated § 75a-3-106(2)(b)(i): is acting under the supervision of an individual described in Subsection (2)(a); and
Utah Code Annotated § 75a-3-106(2)(b)(ii): is:
Utah Code Annotated § 75a-3-106(2)(b)(ii)(A): a nurse, licensed under Title 58, Chapter 31b, Nurse Practice Act;
Utah Code Annotated § 75a-3-106(2)(b)(ii)(B): a physician assistant, licensed under Title 58, Chapter 70a, Utah Physician Assistant Act;
Utah Code Annotated § 75a-3-106(2)(b)(ii)(C): a mental health professional, licensed under Title 58, Chapter 60, Mental Health Professional Practice Act; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75a-3-106(2)(b)(ii)(D): another health care provider, designated by rule as described in Subsection (10).
Utah Code Annotated § 75a-3-106(3): 75A-3-206; 75A-3-206 An order for life sustaining treatment shall be signed:
Utah Code Annotated § 75a-3-106(3)(a): personally, by the physician, APRN, or physician assistant of the individual to whom the order for life sustaining treatment relates; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75a-3-106(3)(b): 75A-3-206; 75A-3-206
Utah Code Annotated § 75a-3-106(3)(b)(i): if the individual to whom the order for life sustaining treatment relates is an adult with health care decision making capacity, by:
Utah Code Annotated § 75a-3-106(3)(b)(i)(A): the individual; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75a-3-106(3)(b)(i)(B): an adult who is directed by the individual to sign the order for life sustaining treatment on behalf of the individual;
Utah Code Annotated § 75a-3-106(3)(b)(ii): 75A-3-206; 75A-3-206 if the individual to whom the order for life sustaining treatment relates is an adult who lacks health care decision making capacity, by:
Utah Code Annotated § 75a-3-106(3)(b)(ii)(A): 75A-3-206 the surrogate with the highest priority under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75a-3-106(3)(b)(ii)(B): 75A-3-206 the majority of the class of surrogates with the highest priority under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75a-3-106(3)(b)(ii)(C): an individual directed to sign the order for life sustaining treatment by, and on behalf of, the individuals described in Subsection (3)(b)(ii)(A) or (B); or
Utah Code Annotated § 75a-3-106(3)(b)(iii): if the individual to whom the order for life sustaining treatment relates is a minor, by a parent or guardian of the minor.
Utah Code Annotated § 75a-3-106(4): If an order for life sustaining treatment relates to a minor and directs that life sustaining treatment be withheld or withdrawn from the minor, the order shall include a certification by two physicians that, in their clinical judgment, an order to withhold or withdraw life sustaining treatment is in the best interest of the minor.
Utah Code Annotated § 75a-3-106(5): An order for life sustaining treatment:
Utah Code Annotated § 75a-3-106(5)(a): shall be in writing, on a form designated by the Department of Health and Human Services;
Utah Code Annotated § 75a-3-106(5)(b): shall state the date on which the order for life sustaining treatment was made;
Utah Code Annotated § 75a-3-106(5)(c): may specify the level of life sustaining care to be provided to the individual to whom the order relates; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75a-3-106(5)(d): may direct that life sustaining care be withheld or withdrawn from the individual to whom the order relates.
Utah Code Annotated § 75a-3-106(6): A health care provider or emergency medical service provider, licensed or certified under Title 53, Chapter 2d, Emergency Medical Services Act, is immune from civil or criminal liability, and is not subject to discipline for unprofessional conduct, for:
Utah Code Annotated § 75a-3-106(6)(a): complying with an order for life sustaining treatment in good faith; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75a-3-106(6)(b): providing life sustaining treatment to an individual when an order for life sustaining treatment directs that the life sustaining treatment be withheld or withdrawn.
Utah Code Annotated § 75a-3-106(7): 75A-3-301 To the extent that the provisions of an order for life sustaining treatment described in this section conflict with the provisions of an advance health care directive made under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75a-3-106(8): An adult, or a parent or guardian of a minor, may revoke an order for life sustaining treatment by:
Utah Code Annotated § 75a-3-106(8)(a): orally informing emergency service personnel;
Utah Code Annotated § 75a-3-106(8)(b): writing "void" across the order for life sustaining treatment form;
Utah Code Annotated § 75a-3-106(8)(c): burning, tearing, or otherwise destroying or defacing:
Utah Code Annotated § 75a-3-106(8)(c)(i): the order for life sustaining treatment form; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75a-3-106(8)(c)(ii): a bracelet or other evidence of the order for life sustaining treatment;
Utah Code Annotated § 75a-3-106(8)(d): asking another adult to take the action described in this Subsection (8) on the individual's behalf;
Utah Code Annotated § 75a-3-106(8)(e): signing or directing another adult to sign a written revocation on the individual's behalf;
Utah Code Annotated § 75a-3-106(8)(f): stating, in the presence of an adult witness, that the individual wishes to revoke the order; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75a-3-106(8)(g): completing a new order for life sustaining treatment.
Utah Code Annotated § 75a-3-106(9): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75a-3-106(9)(a): Except as provided in Subsection (9)(c), a surrogate for an adult who lacks health care decision making capacity may only revoke an order for life sustaining treatment if the revocation is consistent with the substituted judgment standard.
Utah Code Annotated § 75a-3-106(9)(b): Except as provided in Subsection (9)(c), a surrogate who has authority under this section to sign an order for life sustaining treatment may revoke an order for life sustaining treatment, in accordance with Subsection (9)(a), by:
Utah Code Annotated § 75a-3-106(9)(b)(i): signing a written revocation of the order for life sustaining treatment; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75a-3-106(9)(b)(ii): completing and signing a new order for life sustaining treatment.
Utah Code Annotated § 75a-3-106(9)(c): A surrogate may not revoke an order for life sustaining treatment during the period of time beginning when an emergency service provider is contacted for assistance, and ending when the emergency ends.
Utah Code Annotated § 75a-3-106(10): 75A-3-303
Utah Code Annotated § 75a-3-106(10)(a): 75A-3-303 The Department of Health and Human Services shall make rules, in accordance with Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act, to:

Utah Code Annotated § 75a-3-106(10)(c): The Department of Health and Human Services may assist others with training of health care professionals regarding this chapter.

Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-107(7): 75A-3-203 an individual who meets the requirements of Section


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-201 Capacity to make health care decisions -- Presumption -- Overcoming presumption.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-201(1): An adult is presumed to have:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-201(1)(a): health care decision making capacity; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-201(1)(b): capacity to make or revoke an advance health care directive.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-201(2): To overcome the presumption of capacity described in Subsection (1)(a), a physician, an APRN, or a physician assistant who has personally examined the adult and assessed the adult's health care decision making capacity must:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-201(2)(a): find that the adult lacks health care decision making capacity;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-201(2)(b): record the finding in the adult's medical chart including an indication of whether the adult is likely to regain health care decision making capacity; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-201(2)(c): make a reasonable effort to communicate the determination to:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-201(2)(c)(i): the adult;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-201(2)(c)(ii): other health care providers or health care facilities that the person who makes the finding would routinely inform of such a finding; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-201(2)(c)(iii): if the adult has a surrogate, any known surrogate.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-201(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-201(3)(a): An adult who is found to lack health care decision making capacity in accordance with Subsection (2) may, at any time, challenge the finding by:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-201(3)(a)(i): submitting to a health care provider a written notice stating that the adult disagrees with the physician's or physician assistant's finding; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-201(3)(a)(ii): orally informing the health care provider that the adult disagrees with the finding.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-201(3)(b): A health care provider who is informed of a challenge under Subsection (3)(a), shall, if the adult has a surrogate, promptly inform the surrogate of the adult's challenge.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-201(3)(c): A surrogate informed of a challenge to a finding under this section, or the adult if no surrogate is acting on the adult's behalf, shall inform the following of the adult's challenge:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-201(3)(c)(i): any other health care providers involved in the adult's care; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-201(3)(c)(ii): the health care facility, if any, in which the adult is receiving care.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-201(3)(d): Unless otherwise ordered by a court, a finding, under Subsection (2), that the adult lacks health care decision making capacity, is not in effect if the adult challenges the finding under Subsection (3)(a).
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-201(3)(e): If an adult does not challenge the finding described in Subsection (2), the health care provider and health care facility may rely on a surrogate, pursuant to the provisions of this chapter, to make health care decisions for the adult.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-201(4): A health care provider or health care facility that relies on a surrogate to make decisions on behalf of an adult has an ongoing obligation to consider whether the adult continues to lack health care decision making capacity.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-201(5): If at any time a health care provider finds, based on an examination and assessment, that the adult has regained health care decision making capacity, the health care provider shall record the results of the assessment in the adult's medical record, and the adult can direct the adult's own health care.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-202 Effect of current health care preferences -- Health care decision making.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-202(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-202(1)(a): An adult with health care decision making capacity retains the right to make health care decisions as long as the adult has health care decision making capacity.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-202(1)(b): For purposes of this chapter, the inability to communicate through speech does not mean that the adult lacks health care decision making capacity.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-202(2): An adult's current health care decisions, however expressed or indicated, always supersede an adult's prior decisions or health care directives.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-202(3): 75A-3-201; 75A-3-201 Unless otherwise directed in an advance health care directive, an advance health care directive or the authority of a surrogate to make health care decisions on behalf of an adult:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-202(3)(a): 75A-3-201 is effective only after a physician, physician assistant, or APRN makes a determination of incapacity as provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-202(3)(b): remains in effect during any period of time in which the declarant lacks capacity to make health care decisions; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-202(3)(c): 75A-3-201 ceases to be effective when:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-202(3)(c)(i): a declarant disqualifies a surrogate or revokes the advance health care directive;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-202(3)(c)(ii): a health care provider finds that the declarant has health care decision making capacity;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-202(3)(c)(iii): a court issues an order invalidating a health care directive; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-202(3)(c)(iv): 75A-3-201 the declarant has challenged the finding of incapacity under the provisions of Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-203 Default surrogates.
---------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-203(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-203(1)(a): Any member of the class described in Subsection (1)(b) may act as an adult's surrogate if:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-203(1)(a)(i): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-203(1)(a)(i)(A): the adult has not appointed an agent;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-203(1)(a)(i)(B): an appointed agent is not reasonably available; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-203(1)(a)(i)(C): a guardian has not been appointed; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-203(1)(a)(ii): the member of the class described in Subsection (1)(b) is:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-203(1)(a)(ii)(A): over 18 years old;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-203(1)(a)(ii)(B): has health care decision making capacity;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-203(1)(a)(ii)(C): is reasonably available; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-203(1)(a)(ii)(D): has not been disqualified by the adult or a court.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-203(1)(b): Except as provided in Subsection (1)(a), and subject to Subsection (1)(c), the following classes of the adult's family, in descending order of priority, may act as the adult's surrogate:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-203(1)(b)(i): the adult's spouse, unless the adult is divorced or legally separated; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-203(1)(b)(ii): the following family members:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-203(1)(b)(ii)(A): a child;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-203(1)(b)(ii)(B): a parent;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-203(1)(b)(ii)(C): a sibling;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-203(1)(b)(ii)(D): a grandchild; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-203(1)(b)(ii)(E): a grandparent.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-203(1)(c): A person described in Subsection (1)(b), may not direct an adult's care if a person of a higher priority class is able and willing to act as a surrogate for the adult.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-203(1)(d): A court may disqualify a person described in Subsection (1)(b) from acting as a surrogate if the court finds that the person has acted in a manner that is inconsistent with the position of trust in which a surrogate is placed.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-203(2): If the family members designated in Subsection (1)(b) are not reasonably available to act as a surrogate, a person who is 18 years old or older, other than those designated in Subsection (1) may act as a surrogate if the person:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-203(2)(a): has health care decision making capacity;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-203(2)(b): has exhibited special care and concern for the patient;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-203(2)(c): knows the patient and the patient's personal values; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-203(2)(d): is reasonably available to act as a surrogate.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-203(3): The surrogate shall communicate the surrogate's assumption of authority as promptly as practicable to the members of a class who:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-203(3)(a): have an equal or higher priority and are not acting as surrogate; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-203(3)(b): can be readily contacted.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-203(4): A health care provider shall comply with the decision of a majority of the members of the highest priority class who have communicated their views to the provider if:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-203(4)(a): more than one member of the highest priority class assumes authority to act as default surrogate;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-203(4)(b): the members of the class do not agree on a health care decision; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-203(4)(c): the health care provider is informed of the disagreement among the members of the class.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-203(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-203(5)(a): An adult may at any time disqualify a default surrogate, including a member of the adult's family, from acting as the adult's surrogate by:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-203(5)(a)(i): a signed writing;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-203(5)(a)(ii): personally informing a witness of the disqualification; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-203(5)(a)(iii): informing the surrogate of the disqualification.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-203(5)(b): Disqualification of a surrogate is effective even if the adult has been found to lack health care decision making capacity.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-203(6): 75A-3-107 If reasonable doubt exists regarding the status of an adult claiming the right to act as a default surrogate, the health care provider may:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-203(6)(a): require the person to provide a sworn statement giving facts and circumstances reasonably sufficient to establish the claimed authority; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-203(6)(b): 75A-3-107 seek a ruling from the court under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-203(7): 75A-3-107 A health care provider may seek a ruling from a court pursuant to Section


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-204 Surrogate decision making -- Scope of authority.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-204(1): 75A-3-203; 75A-3-301 A surrogate acting under the authority of Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-204(1)(a): the adult's current preferences, to the extent possible;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-204(1)(b): the adult's written or oral health care directions, if any; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-204(1)(c): the substituted judgment standard.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-204(2): 75A-3-203; 75A-3-301 A surrogate acting under the authority of Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-204(2)(a): may not admit the adult to a licensed health care facility for long-term custodial placement other than for assessment, rehabilitative, or respite care over the objection of the adult; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-204(2)(b): may make health care decisions, including decisions to terminate life sustaining treatment for the adult patient in accordance with Subsection (1).
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-204(3): A surrogate acting under authority of this section is not subject to civil or criminal liability or claims of unprofessional conduct for surrogate health care decisions made:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-204(3)(a): in accordance with this section; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-204(3)(b): in good faith.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-205 Health care decisions by guardian.
------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-205(1): A court-appointed guardian shall comply with an adult's advance health care directive and may not revoke the adult's advance health care directive unless the court, for cause, expressly revokes the adult's directive.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-205(2): A health care decision of an agent takes precedence over that of a guardian, in the absence of a court order to the contrary.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-205(3): Except as provided in Subsections (1) and (2), a health care decision made by a guardian for the adult patient is effective without judicial approval.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-205(4): 75A-3-204 A guardian is not subject to civil or criminal liability or to claims of unprofessional conduct for a surrogate health care decision made:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-205(4)(a): in good faith; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-205(4)(b): 75A-3-204 in accordance with Section


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-206 Priority of decision makers.
------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-206(1): 75A-3-201; 75A-3-301; 75A-3-203 The following is the order of priority of those authorized to make health care decisions on behalf of an adult who has been found to lack health care decision making capacity under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-206(1)(a): 75A-3-301 a health care agent appointed by an adult under the provisions of Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-206(1)(a)(i): the adult; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-206(1)(a)(ii): a court of law;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-206(1)(b): a court-appointed guardian; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-206(1)(c): 75A-3-203 the highest priority default surrogate acting under authority of Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-206(2): A health care provider or health care facility obtaining consent for health care from a surrogate shall make a reasonable effort to identify and obtain consent from the surrogate with the highest priority.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-207 Notification to health care provider -- Obligations of health care providers -- Liability.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-207(1): It is the responsibility of the declarant or surrogate, to the extent that the responsibility is not assigned to a health care provider or health care facility by state or federal law, to notify or provide for notification to a health care provider and a health care facility of:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-207(1)(a): the existence of a health care directive;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-207(1)(b): the revocation of a health care directive;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-207(1)(c): the existence or revocation of appointment of an agent or default surrogate;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-207(1)(d): the disqualification of a default surrogate; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-207(1)(e): the appointment or revocation of appointment of a guardian.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-207(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-207(2)(a): A health care provider or health care facility is not subject to civil or criminal liability or to claims of unprofessional conduct for failing to act upon a health care directive, a revocation of a health care directive, or a disqualification of a surrogate until the health care provider or health care facility has received an oral directive from an adult or a copy of a written directive or revocation of the health care directive, or the disqualification of the surrogate.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-207(2)(b): A health care provider and health care facility that is notified under Subsection (1) shall include in the adult patient's medical record:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-207(2)(b)(i): the health care directive or a copy of it, a revocation of a health care directive, or a disqualification of a surrogate; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-207(2)(b)(ii): the date, time, and place in which any written or oral notice of the document described in this Subsection (2)(b) is received.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-207(3): 75A-3-107 A health care provider or health care facility acting in good faith and in accordance with generally accepted health care standards is not subject to civil or criminal liability or to discipline for unprofessional conduct for:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-207(3)(a): complying with a health care decision made by an adult with health care decision making capacity;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-207(3)(b): complying with a health care decision made by a surrogate apparently having authority to make a health care decision for a person, including a decision to withhold or withdraw health care;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-207(3)(c): declining to comply with a health care decision of a surrogate based on a belief that the surrogate then lacked authority;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-207(3)(d): declining to comply with a health care decision of an adult who lacks decision making capacity;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-207(3)(e): 75A-3-107 seeking a judicial determination, or requiring a surrogate to obtain a judicial determination, under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-207(3)(e)(i): the validity of a health care directive;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-207(3)(e)(ii): the validity of directions from a surrogate or guardian;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-207(3)(e)(iii): the decision making capacity of an adult who challenges a physician's finding of incapacity; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-207(3)(e)(iv): the authority of a guardian or surrogate; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-207(3)(f): complying with an advance health care directive and assuming that the directive was valid when made, and has not been revoked or terminated.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-207(4): 75A-3-203
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-207(4)(a): Health care providers and health care facilities shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-207(4)(a)(i): cooperate with a person authorized under this chapter to make written directives concerning health care;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-207(4)(a)(ii): unless the provisions of Subsection (4)(b) apply, comply with:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-207(4)(a)(ii)(A): a health care decision of an adult; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-207(4)(a)(ii)(B): a health care decision made by the highest ranking surrogate then authorized to make health care decisions for an adult, to the same extent as if the decision had been made by the adult;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-207(4)(a)(iii): before implementing a health care decision made by a surrogate, make a reasonable attempt to communicate to the adult on whose behalf the decision is made:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-207(4)(a)(iii)(A): the decision made; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-207(4)(a)(iii)(B): the identity of the surrogate making the decision.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-207(4)(b): 75A-3-203 A health care provider or health care facility may decline to comply with a health care decision if:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-207(4)(b)(i): 75A-3-203 in the opinion of the health care provider:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-207(4)(b)(i)(A): the adult who made the decision lacks health care decision making capacity;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-207(4)(b)(i)(B): the surrogate who made the decision lacks health care decision making capacity;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-207(4)(b)(i)(C): the health care provider has evidence that the surrogate's instructions are inconsistent with the adult's health care instructions, or, for a person who has always lacked health care decision making capacity, that the surrogate's instructions are inconsistent with the best interest of the adult; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-207(4)(b)(i)(D): 75A-3-203 there is reasonable doubt regarding the status of a person claiming the right to act as a default surrogate, in which case the health care provider shall comply with Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-207(4)(b)(ii): the health care provider declines to comply for reasons of conscience.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-207(4)(c): A health care provider or health care facility that declines to comply with a health care decision in accordance with Subsection (4)(b) must:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-207(4)(c)(i): promptly inform the adult and any acting surrogate of the reason for refusing to comply with the health care decision;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-207(4)(c)(ii): make a good faith attempt to resolve the conflict; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-207(4)(c)(iii): provide continuing care to the patient until the issue is resolved or until a transfer can be made to a health care provider or health care facility that will implement the requested instruction or decision.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-207(4)(d): A health care provider or health care facility that declines to comply with a health care instruction, after meeting the obligations set forth in Subsection (4)(c) may transfer the adult to a health care provider or health care facility that will carry out the requested health care decisions.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-207(4)(e): A health care facility may decline to follow a health care decision for reasons of conscience under Subsection (4)(b)(ii) if:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-207(4)(e)(i): the health care decision is contrary to a policy of the facility that is expressly based on reasons of conscience;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-207(4)(e)(ii): the policy was timely communicated to the adult and an adult's surrogate;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-207(4)(e)(iii): the facility promptly informs the adult, if possible, and any surrogate then authorized to make decisions for the adult;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-207(4)(e)(iv): the facility provides continuing care to the adult until a transfer can be made to a health care facility that will implement the requested instruction or decision; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-207(4)(e)(v): unless an adult or surrogate then authorized to make health care decisions for the adult refuses assistance, immediately make all reasonable efforts to assist in the transfer of the adult to another health care facility that will carry out the instructions or decisions.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-207(5): A health care provider and health care facility:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-207(5)(a): may not require or prohibit the creation or revocation of an advance health care directive as a condition for providing health care; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-207(5)(b): shall comply with all state and federal laws and regulations governing advance health care directives.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-208 Personal representative status.
---------------------------------------------------------------
A surrogate becomes a personal representative for an adult under the Health Insurance Portability and Accountability Act of 1996 when:Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-208(1): 75A-3-201 the adult has been found to lack health care decision making capacity under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-208(2): the adult grants current authority to the surrogate either:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-208(2)(a): in writing; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-208(2)(b): by other expression before a witness who is not the surrogate or agent; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-208(3): the court appoints a guardian authorized to make health care decisions on behalf of the adult.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-301 Advance health care directive -- Appointment of agent -- Powers of agent.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-301(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-301(1)(a): An adult may make an advance health care directive in which the adult may:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-301(1)(a)(i): appoint a health care agent or choose not to appoint a health care agent;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-301(1)(a)(ii): give directions for the care of the adult after the adult loses health care decision making capacity;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-301(1)(a)(iii): choose not to give directions;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-301(1)(a)(iv): state conditions that must be met before life sustaining treatment may be withheld or withdrawn;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-301(1)(a)(v): authorize an agent to consent to the adult's participation in medical research;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-301(1)(a)(vi): nominate a guardian;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-301(1)(a)(vii): authorize an agent to consent to organ donation;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-301(1)(a)(viii): expand or limit the powers of a health care agent; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-301(1)(a)(ix): designate the agent's access to the adult's medical records.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-301(1)(b): An advance health care directive may be oral or written.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-301(1)(c): An advance health care directive shall be witnessed by a disinterested adult.  The witness may not be:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-301(1)(c)(i): the person who signed the directive on behalf of the declarant;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-301(1)(c)(ii): related to the declarant by blood or marriage;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-301(1)(c)(iii): entitled to any portion of the declarant's estate according to the laws of intestate succession of this state or under any will or codicil of the declarant;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-301(1)(c)(iv): the beneficiary of any of the following that are held, owned, made, or established by, or on behalf of, the declarant:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-301(1)(c)(iv)(A): a life insurance policy;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-301(1)(c)(iv)(B): a trust;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-301(1)(c)(iv)(C): a qualified plan;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-301(1)(c)(iv)(D): a pay on death account; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-301(1)(c)(iv)(E): a transfer on death deed;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-301(1)(c)(v): entitled to benefit financially upon the death of the declarant;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-301(1)(c)(vi): entitled to a right to, or interest in, real or personal property upon the death of the declarant;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-301(1)(c)(vii): directly financially responsible for the declarant's medical care;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-301(1)(c)(viii): a health care provider who is:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-301(1)(c)(viii)(A): providing care to the declarant; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-301(1)(c)(viii)(B): an administrator at a health care facility in which the declarant is receiving care; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-301(1)(c)(ix): the appointed agent.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-301(1)(d): The witness to an oral advance health care directive shall state the circumstances under which the directive was made.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-301(2): An agent appointed under the provisions of this section may not be a health care provider for the declarant, or an owner, operator, or employee of the health care facility at which the declarant is receiving care unless the agent is related to the declarant by blood, marriage, or adoption.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-302 Capacity to complete an advance health care directive.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-302(1): An adult is presumed to have the capacity to complete an advance health care directive.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-302(2): 75A-3-201; 75A-3-303; 75A-3-303 An adult who is found to lack health care decision making capacity under the provisions of Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-302(2)(a): 75A-3-303 lacks the capacity to give an advance health care directive, including Part II of the form created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-302(2)(b): 75A-3-303 may retain the capacity to appoint an agent and complete Part I of the form created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-302(3): The following factors shall be considered by a health care provider, attorney, or court when determining whether an adult described in Subsection (2)(b) has retained the capacity to appoint an agent:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-302(3)(a): whether the adult has expressed over time an intent to appoint the same person as agent;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-302(3)(b): whether the choice of agent is consistent with past relationships and patterns of behavior between the adult and the prospective agent, or, if inconsistent, whether there is a reasonable justification for the change; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-302(3)(c): whether the adult's expression of the intent to appoint the agent occurs at times when, or in settings where, the adult has the greatest ability to make and communicate decisions.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-303 Optional form for advance health care directive.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
I do not want to choose an agent.Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-303(1): (2) The form created in Subsection
