Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-304 Presumption of validity of advance health care directive.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-304(1): An advance health care directive executed under this chapter is presumed valid and binding.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-304(2): A health care provider and a health care facility, in the absence of notice to the contrary, shall presume that a declarant who executed an advance health care directive, whether or not in the presence of a health care provider, had the required decision making capacity at the time the declarant signed the directive.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-304(3): The fact that a declarant executed an advance health care directive shall not be construed as an indication that the declarant was suffering from mental illness or lacked decision making capacity.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-305 Advance health care directive effect on insurance policies.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-305(1): If an adult makes an advance health care directive under this chapter, the advance health care directive does not affect in any manner:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-305(1)(a): the obligation of any life or medical insurance company regarding any policy of life or medical insurance;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-305(1)(b): the sale, procurement, or issuance of any policy of life or health insurance; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-305(1)(c): the terms of any existing policy.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-305(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-305(2)(a): Notwithstanding any terms of an insurance policy to the contrary, an insurance policy is not legally impaired or invalidated in any manner by:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-305(2)(a)(i): withholding or withdrawing life sustaining procedures; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-305(2)(a)(ii): following directions in an advance health care directive executed as provided in this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-305(2)(b): Following health care instructions in an advance health care directive does not constitute legal cause for failing to pay life or health insurance benefits.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-305(2)(c): Death that occurs after following the instructions of an advance health care directive or a surrogate's instructions does not for any purpose constitute a suicide or homicide or legally impair or invalidate a policy of insurance or an annuity providing a death benefit.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-305(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-305(3)(a): The following may not require an adult to execute an advance health care directive or to make any particular choices or entries in an advance health care directive under this chapter as a condition for being insured for or receiving health care or life insurance contract services:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-305(3)(a)(i): a health care provider;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-305(3)(a)(ii): a health care facility;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-305(3)(a)(iii): a health maintenance organization;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-305(3)(a)(iv): an insurer issuing disability, health, or life insurance;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-305(3)(a)(v): a self-insured employee welfare or benefit plan;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-305(3)(a)(vi): a nonprofit medical service corporation or mutual nonprofit hospital service corporation; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-305(3)(a)(vii): any other person, firm, or entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-305(3)(b): Nothing in this chapter:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-305(3)(b)(i): may be construed to require an insurer to insure risks otherwise considered by the insurer as not a covered risk;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-305(3)(b)(ii): is intended to impair or supersede any other legal right or legal responsibility which an adult may have to effect the withholding or withdrawal of life sustaining procedures in any lawful manner; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-305(3)(b)(iii): creates any presumption concerning the intention of an adult who has not executed an advance health care directive.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-306 Advance health care directive effect during pregnancy.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-306(1): An advance health care directive that provides for the withholding or withdrawal of life sustaining procedures has no force during the course of a declarant's pregnancy.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-306(2): Subsection (1) does not negate the appointment of a health care agent during the course of a declarant's pregnancy.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-307 Revocation of advance health care directive.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-307(1): An advance health care directive may be revoked at any time by the declarant by:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-307(1)(a): writing "void" across the document;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-307(1)(b): obliterating, burning, tearing, or otherwise destroying or defacing the document in any manner indicating an intent to revoke;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-307(1)(c): instructing another to do one of the acts described in Subsection (1)(a) or (b);
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-307(1)(d): a written revocation of the directive signed and dated by:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-307(1)(d)(i): the declarant; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-307(1)(d)(ii): an adult:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-307(1)(d)(ii)(A): signing on behalf of the declarant; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-307(1)(d)(ii)(B): acting at the direction of the declarant; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-307(1)(e): an oral expression of an intent to revoke the directive in the presence of a witness who is age 18 years old or older and who is not:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-307(1)(e)(i): related to the declarant by blood or marriage;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-307(1)(e)(ii): entitled to any portion of the declarant's estate according to the laws of intestate succession of this state or under any will or codicil of the declarant;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-307(1)(e)(iii): the beneficiary of any of the following that are held, owned, made, or established by, or on behalf of, the declarant:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-307(1)(e)(iii)(A): a life insurance policy;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-307(1)(e)(iii)(B): a trust;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-307(1)(e)(iii)(C): a qualified plan;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-307(1)(e)(iii)(D): a pay on death account; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-307(1)(e)(iii)(E): a transfer on death deed;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-307(1)(e)(iv): entitled to benefit financially upon the death of the declarant;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-307(1)(e)(v): entitled to a right to, or interest in, real or personal property upon the death of the declarant;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-307(1)(e)(vi): directly financially responsible for the declarant's medical care;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-307(1)(e)(vii): a health care provider who is:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-307(1)(e)(vii)(A): providing care to the declarant; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-307(1)(e)(vii)(B): an administrator at a health care facility in which the declarant is receiving care; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-307(1)(e)(viii): the adult who will become agent or default surrogate after the revocation.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-307(2): A decree of annulment, divorce, dissolution of marriage, or legal separation revokes the designation of a spouse as an agent, unless:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-307(2)(a): otherwise specified in the decree; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-307(2)(b): the declarant has affirmed the intent to retain the agent subsequent to the annulment, divorce, or legal separation.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-307(3): An advance health care directive that conflicts with an earlier advance health care directive revokes the earlier directive to the extent of the conflict.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-308 Illegal destruction or falsification of advance health care directive.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-308(1): A person is guilty of a class B misdemeanor if the person:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-308(1)(a): willfully conceals, cancels, defaces, obliterates, or damages an advance health care directive of another without the declarant's consent; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-308(1)(b): falsifies, forges, or alters a health care directive or a revocation of the advance health care directive of another person.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-308(2): A person is guilty of criminal homicide if:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-308(2)(a): the person:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-308(2)(a)(i): falsifies or forges the advance health care directive of an adult; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-308(2)(a)(ii): willfully conceals or withholds personal knowledge of:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-308(2)(a)(ii)(A): the existence of an advance health care directive;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-308(2)(a)(ii)(B): the revocation of an advance health care directive; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-308(2)(a)(ii)(C): the disqualification of a surrogate; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-308(2)(b): the actions described in Subsection (2)(a) cause a withholding or withdrawal of life sustaining procedures contrary to the wishes of a declarant resulting in the death of the declarant.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-309 Reciprocity of advance health care directive -- Application of former provisions of law.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Unless otherwise provided in the advance health care directive:Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-309(1): a health care provider or health care facility may, in good faith, rely on any advance health care directive, power of attorney, or similar instrument:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-309(1)(a): executed in another state; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-309(1)(b): executed prior to January 1, 2008, in this state;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-309(2): an advance health care directive executed under the provisions of this chapter shall be governed pursuant to the provisions of this chapter that were in effect at that time, unless it appears from the directive that the declarant intended the current provisions of this chapter to apply; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-3-309(3): the advance health care directive described in Subsection (1) is presumed to comply with the requirements of this chapter.


Utah Code Annotated - Title 75A - Chapter 4 - Uniform Powers of Appointment Act
*******************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-101 Reserved.
-----------------------------------------
Reserved.

Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-102 Definitions for chapter.
--------------------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-102(1): "Appointee" means a person to which a powerholder makes an appointment of appointive property.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-102(2): "Appointive property" means the property or property interest subject to a power of appointment.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-102(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-102(3)(a): "Blanket-exercise clause" means a clause in an instrument that exercises a power of appointment and is not a specific-exercise clause.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-102(3)(b): "Blanket-exercise clause" includes a clause that:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-102(3)(b)(i): expressly uses the words "any power" in exercising any power of appointment the powerholder has;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-102(3)(b)(ii): expressly uses the words "any property" in appointing any property over which the powerholder has a power of appointment; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-102(3)(b)(iii): disposes of all property subject to disposition by the powerholder.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-102(4): 75-1-201 "Descendant" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-102(5): "Donor" means a person that creates a power of appointment.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-102(6): 75-1-201 "Estate" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-102(7): "Exclusionary power of appointment" means a power of appointment exercisable in favor of any one or more of the permissible appointees to the exclusion of the other permissible appointees.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-102(8): "General power of appointment" means a power of appointment exercisable in favor of the powerholder, the powerholder's estate, a creditor of the powerholder, or a creditor of the powerholder's estate.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-102(9): "Gift-in-default clause" means a clause identifying a taker in default of appointment.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-102(10): "Impermissible appointee" means a person that is not a permissible appointee.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-102(11): "Instrument" means a record.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-102(12): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-102(12)(a): "Nongeneral power of appointment" means a power of appointment that is not a general power of appointment.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-102(12)(b): "Nongeneral power of appointment" includes a special power of appointment, a limited power of appointment, or similar terminology that is used in an instrument creating a power that does not grant powers making it a general power of appointment.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-102(13): "Permissible appointee" means a person in whose favor a powerholder may exercise a power of appointment.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-102(14): "Person" means an individual, estate, trust, business or nonprofit entity, public corporation, government or governmental subdivision, agency, instrumentality, or other legal entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-102(15): "Powerholder" means a person in whom a donor creates a power of appointment.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-102(16): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-102(16)(a): "Power of appointment" means a power that enables a powerholder acting in a nonfiduciary capacity to designate a recipient of an interest in, or another power of appointment over, the appointive property.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-102(16)(b): "Power of appointment" does not include a power of attorney.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-102(17): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-102(17)(a): "Presently exercisable power of appointment" means a power of appointment exercisable by the powerholder at a relevant time.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-102(17)(b): "Presently exercisable power of appointment" includes a power of appointment not exercisable until the occurrence of a specified event, the satisfaction of an ascertainable standard, or the passage of a specified time only after:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-102(17)(b)(i): the occurrence of the specified event;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-102(17)(b)(ii): the satisfaction of the ascertainable standard; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-102(17)(b)(iii): the passage of the specified time.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-102(17)(c): "Presently exercisable power of appointment" does not include a power exercisable only at the powerholder's death.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-102(18): 75-1-201 "Property" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-102(19): "Record" means information that is inscribed on a tangible medium or that is stored in an electronic or other medium and is retrievable in perceivable form.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-102(20): "Specific-exercise clause" means a clause in an instrument that specifically refers to and exercises a particular power of appointment.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-102(21): "Taker in default of appointment" means a person that takes all or part of the appointive property to the extent the powerholder does not effectively exercise the power of appointment.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-102(22): "Terms of the instrument" means the manifestation of the intent of the maker of the instrument regarding the instrument's provisions as expressed in the instrument or as may be established by other evidence that would be admissible in a legal proceeding.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-102(23): 75-1-201 "Trust" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-102(24): 75-1-201 "Will" means the same as that term is defined in Section


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-103 Governing law.
----------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-103(1): Unless the terms of the instrument creating a power of appointment manifest a contrary intent:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-103(1)(a): the creation, revocation, amendment, interpretation and definition of terms, or the determination of the rights of the appointee of the power is governed by the law of the donor's domicile at the relevant time; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-103(1)(b): the formalities for the exercise, release, or disclaimer of the power, or the revocation or amendment of the exercise, release, or disclaimer of the power is governed by the law of the powerholder's state of domicile at the relevant time.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-103(2): The law of the powerholder's state of domicile may not govern the interpretation and definition of terms, or the determination of the rights of the appointee of the power, which shall be governed by the law of the donor's domicile at the relevant time.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-103(3): 75A-4-502 Claims of creditors, including creditor claims regarding a power not created by a powerholder as set forth in Section


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-104 Common law and principles of equity.
--------------------------------------------------------------------
The common law and principles of equity supplement this chapter, except to the extent modified by this chapter or laws of this state other than this chapter.

Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-201 Creation of power of appointment.
-----------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-201(1): A power of appointment is created only if:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-201(1)(a): the instrument creating the power is valid under applicable law; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-201(1)(b): the terms of the instrument creating the power manifest the donor's intent to create in a powerholder a power of appointment over the appointive property exercisable in favor of a permissible appointee.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-201(2): A power of appointment may be created by the exercise of a power of appointment.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-201(3): A power of appointment may not be created in a deceased individual.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-201(4): Subject to an applicable rule against perpetuities, a power of appointment may be created in an unborn or unascertained powerholder.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-202 Nontransferability.
---------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-202(1): A powerholder may not transfer a power of appointment.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-202(2): If a powerholder dies without exercising or releasing a power, the power lapses.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-203 Presumption of unlimited authority.
-------------------------------------------------------------------
Subject to SectionUtah Code Annotated § 75A-4-203(1): presently exercisable;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-203(2): exclusionary; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-203(3): 75A-4-204 except as otherwise provided in Section


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-204 Exception to presumption of unlimited authority.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Unless the terms of the instrument creating a power of appointment manifest a contrary intent, the power is nongeneral if:Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-204(1): the power is exercisable only at the powerholder's death; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-204(2): the permissible appointees of the power are a defined and limited class that does not include the powerholder's estate, the powerholder's creditors, or the creditors of the powerholder's estate.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-205 Rules of classification.
--------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-205(1): As used in this section, "adverse party" means a person with a substantial beneficial interest in property that would be affected adversely by a powerholder's exercise or nonexercise of a power of appointment in favor of the powerholder, the powerholder's estate, a creditor of the powerholder, or a creditor of the powerholder's estate.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-205(2): If a powerholder may exercise a power of appointment only with the consent or joinder of an adverse party, the power is nongeneral.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-205(3): If the permissible appointees of a power of appointment are not defined and limited, the power is exclusionary.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-206 Donor's power to revoke or amend.
-----------------------------------------------------------------
A donor may revoke or amend a power of appointment unless or to the extent the instrument creating the power is made irrevocable by the donor or the exercise of a presently exercisable power has been irrevocably made or effected.

Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-301 Requisites for exercise of power of appointment.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
A power of appointment is exercised only:Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-301(1): if the instrument exercising the power is valid under applicable law;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-301(2): if the terms of the instrument exercising the power:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-301(2)(a): manifest the powerholder's intent to exercise the power; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-301(2)(b): satisfy the requirements of exercise, if any, imposed by the donor; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-301(3): to the extent the appointment is a permissible exercise of the power.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-302 Intent to exercise -- Determining intent from residuary clause.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-302(1): As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-302(1)(a): "Residuary clause" does not include a residuary clause containing a blanket-exercise clause or a specific-exercise clause.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-302(1)(b): "Will" includes a codicil and a testamentary instrument that revises another will.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-302(2): A residuary clause in a powerholder's will, or a comparable clause in the powerholder's revocable trust, manifests the powerholder's intent to exercise a power of appointment only if:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-302(2)(a): the terms of the instrument containing the residuary clause do not manifest a contrary intent;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-302(2)(b): the power is a general power exercisable in favor of the powerholder's estate;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-302(2)(c): there is no gift-in-default clause or the clause is ineffective; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-302(2)(d): the powerholder did not release the power.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-303 Intent to exercise -- After-acquired power.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------
Unless the terms of the instrument exercising a power of appointment manifest a contrary intent:Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-303(1): except as otherwise provided in Subsection (2), a blanket-exercise clause extends to a power acquired by the powerholder after executing the instrument containing the clause; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-303(2): if the powerholder is also the donor of the power, the clause does not extend to the power unless there is no gift-in-default clause or the gift-in-default clause is ineffective.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-304 Compliance with donor-imposed formal requirements.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-304(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-304(1)(a): A powerholder's compliance with formal requirements of appointment imposed by the donor is sufficient only if the powerholder substantially complies with the conditions, requirements, and formalities set forth in the power of appointment, including complying with all the requirements for making specific reference to the power, that the power shall be exercised in a specific document such as a will, or that the document exercising the power shall be witnessed or notarized.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-304(1)(b): If the donor limited the powerholder's exercise to a validly executed will, substantial compliance may not include the exercise of the power by a trust or another document not meeting the requirements of a properly executed will.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-304(2): Unless required by the instrument creating the power, the probate of a properly executed will is not required for the exercise of a power to be valid and complete.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-305 Permissible appointment.
--------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-305(1): A powerholder of a general power of appointment that permits appointment to the powerholder or the powerholder's estate may make any appointment, including an appointment in trust or creating a new power of appointment, that the powerholder could make in disposing of the powerholder's own property.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-305(2): A powerholder of a general power of appointment that permits appointment only to the creditors of the powerholder or of the powerholder's estate may appoint only to those creditors.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-305(3): Unless the terms of the instrument creating a power of appointment manifest a contrary intent, the powerholder of a nongeneral power may:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-305(3)(a): make an appointment in any form, including an appointment in trust, in favor of a permissible appointee;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-305(3)(b): create a general power in a permissible appointee;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-305(3)(c): create a nongeneral power in any person to appoint one or more of the permissible appointees of the original nongeneral power; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-305(3)(d): create a nongeneral power in a permissible appointee to appoint one or more persons if the permissible appointees of the new nongeneral power include the permissible appointees of the original nongeneral power.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-306 Appointment to deceased appointee or permissible appointee's descendant.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-306(1): 75-2-603; 75-2-604 Subject to Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-306(2): Unless the terms of the instrument creating a power of appointment manifest a contrary intent, a powerholder of a nongeneral power may exercise the power in favor of, or create a new power of appointment in, a descendant of a deceased permissible appointee whether or not the descendant is described by the donor as a permissible appointee.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-307 Impermissible appointment.
----------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-307(1): 75A-4-306 Except as otherwise provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-307(2): An exercise of a power of appointment in favor of a permissible appointee is ineffective to the extent the appointment is a fraud on the power.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-308 Elective allocation doctrine.
-------------------------------------------------------------
If a powerholder exercises a power of appointment in a disposition that also disposes of property the powerholder owns, the owned property and the appointive property shall be allocated in the permissible manner that best carries out the powerholder's intent.

Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-309 Capture doctrine -- Disposition of ineffectively appointed property under general power.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
To the extent a powerholder of a general power of appointment, other than a power to withdraw property from, revoke, or amend a trust, makes an ineffective appointment:Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-309(1): the gift-in-default clause controls the disposition of the ineffectively appointed property; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-309(2): if there is no gift-in-default clause or to the extent the clause is ineffective, the ineffectively appointed property:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-309(2)(a): passes to:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-309(2)(a)(i): the powerholder if the powerholder is a permissible appointee and is living; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-309(2)(a)(ii): if the powerholder is an impermissible appointee or is deceased, the powerholder's estate if the estate is a permissible appointee; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-309(2)(b): if there is no taker under Subsection (2)(a), passes under a reversionary interest to the donor or the donor's transferee or successor in interest.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-310 Disposition of unappointed property under released or unexercised general power.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
To the extent a powerholder releases or fails to exercise a general power of appointment other than a power to withdraw property from, revoke, or amend a trust:Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-310(1): the gift-in-default clause controls the disposition of the unappointed property; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-310(2): if there is no gift-in-default clause or to the extent the clause is ineffective:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-310(2)(a): except as otherwise provided in Subsection (2)(b), the unappointed property passes to:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-310(2)(a)(i): the powerholder if the powerholder is a permissible appointee and is living; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-310(2)(a)(ii): if the powerholder is an impermissible appointee or is deceased, the powerholder's estate if the estate is a permissible appointee; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-310(2)(b): to the extent the powerholder released the power, or if there is no taker under Subsection (2)(a), the unappointed property passes under a reversionary interest to the donor or the donor's transferee or successor in interest.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-311 Disposition of unappointed property under released or unexercised nongeneral power.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
To the extent a powerholder releases, ineffectively exercises, or fails to exercise a nongeneral power of appointment:Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-311(1): the gift-in-default clause controls the disposition of the unappointed property; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-311(2): if there is no gift-in-default clause or to the extent the clause is ineffective, the unappointed property:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-311(2)(a): passes to the permissible appointees if:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-311(2)(a)(i): the permissible appointees are defined and limited; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-311(2)(a)(ii): the terms of the instrument creating the power do not manifest a contrary intent; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-311(2)(b): if there is no taker under Subsection (2)(a), passes under a reversionary interest to the donor or the donor's transferee or successor in interest.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-312 Disposition of unappointed property if partial appointment to taker in default.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Unless the terms of the instrument creating or exercising a power of appointment manifest a contrary intent, if the powerholder makes a valid partial appointment to a taker in default of appointment, the taker in default of appointment may share fully in unappointed property.

Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-313 Appointment to taker in default.
----------------------------------------------------------------
If a powerholder makes an appointment to a taker in default of appointment and the appointee would have taken the property under a gift-in-default clause had the property not been appointed, the power of appointment is considered not to have been exercised and the appointee takes under the clause.

Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-314 Powerholder's authority to revoke or amend exercise.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Unless the terms of the instrument creating the power of appointment or the instrument exercising the power of appointment provide that the exercise is irrevocable or unamendable, a powerholder may revoke or amend an exercise of a power of appointment made by an instrument effective during the life of the powerholder where the exercise is to become effective at some future time or contingency and where that future time and contingency has not yet occurred, as long as the revocation or amendment is done with the same formality as the original exercise of the power of appointment.

Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-401 Disclaimer.
-------------------------------------------
As provided by SectionUtah Code Annotated § 75A-4-401(1): A powerholder may disclaim all or part of a power of appointment.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-401(2): A permissible appointee, an appointee, or a taker in default of appointment may disclaim all or part of an interest in appointive property.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-402 Authority to release.
-----------------------------------------------------
A powerholder may release a power of appointment, in whole or in part, except to the extent the terms of the instrument creating the power prevent the release.

Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-403 Method of release.
--------------------------------------------------
A powerholder of a releasable power of appointment may release the power in whole or in part:Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-403(1): by substantial compliance with a method provided in the terms of the instrument creating the power; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-403(2): if the terms of the instrument creating the power do not provide a method or the method provided in the terms of the instrument is not expressly made exclusive, by a record manifesting the powerholder's intent by clear and convincing evidence.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-404 Revocation or amendment of release.
-------------------------------------------------------------------
A powerholder may revoke or amend a release of a power of appointment only to the extent that:Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-404(1): the instrument of release is revocable by the powerholder; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-404(2): the powerholder reserves a power of revocation or amendment in the instrument of release.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-405 Power to contract -- Presently exercisable power of appointment.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
A powerholder of a presently exercisable power of appointment may contract:Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-405(1): not to exercise the power; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-405(2): to exercise the power if the contract when made does not confer a benefit on an impermissible appointee.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-406 Power to contract -- Power of appointment not presently exercisable.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
A powerholder of a power of appointment that is not presently exercisable may contract to exercise or not to exercise the power only if the powerholder:Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-406(1): is also the donor of the power; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-406(2): has reserved the power in a revocable trust.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-407 Remedy for breach of contract to appoint or not to appoint.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The remedy for a powerholder's breach of a contract to appoint or not to appoint appointive property is limited to damages payable out of the appointive property or, if appropriate, specific performance of the contract.

Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-501 Creditor claim -- General power created by powerholder.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-501(1): As used in this section, "power of appointment created by the powerholder" includes a power of appointment created in a transfer by another person to the extent the powerholder contributed value to the transfer.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-501(2): Appointive property subject to a general power of appointment created by the powerholder is subject to a claim of a creditor of the powerholder or of the powerholder's estate to the extent provided in Title 25, Chapter 6, Uniform Voidable Transactions Act.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-501(3): Subject to Subsection (2), appointive property subject to a general power of appointment created by the powerholder is not subject to a claim of a creditor of the powerholder or the powerholder's estate to the extent the powerholder irrevocably appointed the property in favor of a person other than the powerholder or the powerholder's estate.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-501(4): Subject to Subsections (2) and (3), and notwithstanding the presence of a spendthrift provision or whether the claim arose before or after the creation of the power of appointment, appointive property subject to a general power of appointment created by the powerholder is subject to a claim of a creditor of:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-501(4)(a): the powerholder, to the same extent as if the powerholder owned the appointive property, if the power is presently exercisable; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-501(4)(b): the powerholder's estate, to the extent the estate is insufficient to satisfy the claim and subject to the right of a decedent to direct the source from which liabilities are paid, if the power is exercisable at the powerholder's death.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-502 Creditor claim -- Power not created by powerholder.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-502(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-502(1)(a): The property subject to a general or a nongeneral power of appointment not created by the powerholder, including a presently exercisable general or nongeneral power of appointment, is exempt from a claim of a creditor of the powerholder or the powerholder's estate.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-502(1)(b): The powerholder of such a power may not be compelled to exercise the power and the powerholder's creditors may not acquire the power, any rights thereto, or reach the trust property or beneficial interests by any other means.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-502(1)(c): A court may not exercise or require the powerholder to exercise the power of appointment.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-502(2): 75A-4-103 As set forth in Section


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-503 Power to withdraw.
--------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-503(1): For purposes of this part, and except as otherwise provided in Subsection (2), a power to withdraw property from a trust is treated, during the time the power may be exercised, as a presently exercisable general power of appointment to the extent of the property subject to the power to withdraw.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-503(2): On the lapse, release, or waiver of a power to withdraw property from a trust, the power is treated as a presently exercisable general power of appointment only to the extent the value of the property affected by the lapse, release, or waiver exceeds the greater of the amount specified in 26 U.S.C. Sec. 2041(b)(2) and 26 U.S.C. Sec. 2514(e) or the amount specified in 26 U.S.C. Sec. 2503(b).


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-601 Uniformity of application and construction.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------
In applying and construing this uniform act, consideration shall be given to the need to promote uniformity of the law with respect to its subject matter among states that enact this uniform law.

Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-602 Relation to Electronic Signatures in Global and National Commerce Act.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
This chapter modifies, limits, or supersedes the Electronic Signatures in Global and National Commerce Act, 15 U.S.C. Sec. 7001 et seq., but does not modify, limit, or supersede Section 101(c) of that act, 15 U.S.C. Sec. 7001(c), or authorize electronic delivery of any of the notices described in Section 103(b) of that act, 15 U.S.C. Sec. 7003(b).

Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-603 Application to existing relationships.
----------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-603(1): Except as otherwise provided in this chapter, on and after May 9, 2017:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-603(1)(a): this chapter applies to a power of appointment created before, on, or after May 9, 2017;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-603(1)(b): this chapter applies to a judicial proceeding concerning a power of appointment commenced on or after May 9, 2017;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-603(1)(c): this chapter applies to a judicial proceeding concerning a power of appointment commenced before May 9, 2017, unless the court finds that application of a particular provision of this chapter would interfere substantially with the effective conduct of the judicial proceeding or prejudice a right of a party, in which case the particular provision of this chapter does not apply and the superseded law applies; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-603(1)(d): a rule of construction or presumption provided in this chapter applies to an instrument executed before May 9, 2017, unless there is a clear indication of a contrary intent in the terms of the instrument.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-603(2): Except as otherwise provided in Subsections (1)(a) through (d), an action done before May 9, 2017, is not affected by this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-4-603(3): If a right is acquired, extinguished, or barred on the expiration of a prescribed period that commenced under law of this state other than this chapter before May 9, 2017, the law continues to apply to the right.

Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-103 Scope.
--------------------------------------
Except as otherwise provided in the terms of a trust or this chapter, this chapter applies to:Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-103(1): a trust or estate; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-103(2): a life estate or other term interest in which the interest of one or more persons will be succeeded by the interest of one or more other persons.

----------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-104(1): 75A-5-103 Except as otherwise provided in the terms of a trust or this chapter, this chapter applies when this state is:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-104(1)(a): the principal place of administration of a trust or estate; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-104(1)(b): 75A-5-103 the situs of property that is not held in a trust or estate and is subject to a life estate or other term interest described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-104(2): By accepting the trusteeship of a trust having the trust's principal place of administration in this state or by moving the principal place of administration of a trust to this state, the trustee submits to the application of this chapter to any matter within the scope of this chapter involving the trust.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-201 Fiduciary duties -- General principles.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-201(1): In making an allocation or determination or exercising discretion under this chapter, a fiduciary shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-201(1)(a): act in good faith, based on what is fair and reasonable to all beneficiaries;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-201(1)(b): administer a trust or estate impartially, except to the extent the terms of the trust manifest an intent that the fiduciary shall or may favor one or more beneficiaries;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-201(1)(c): administer the trust or estate in accordance with the terms of the trust, even if there is a different provision in this chapter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-201(1)(d): administer the trust or estate in accordance with this chapter, except to the extent the terms of the trust provide otherwise or authorize the fiduciary to determine otherwise.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-201(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-201(2)(a): A fiduciary's allocation, determination, or exercise of discretion under this chapter is presumed to be fair and reasonable to all beneficiaries.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-201(2)(b): A fiduciary may exercise a discretionary power of administration given to the fiduciary by the terms of the trust, and an exercise of the power that produces a result different from a result required or permitted by this chapter does not create an inference that the fiduciary abused the fiduciary's discretion.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-201(3): A fiduciary shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-201(3)(a): add a receipt to principal, to the extent neither the terms of the trust nor this chapter allocates the receipt between income and principal; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-201(3)(b): charge a disbursement to principal, to the extent neither the terms of the trust nor this chapter allocates the disbursement between income and principal.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-201(4): 75A-5-203; 75A-5-303; 75A-5-303; 75A-5-303 If a fiduciary determines an exercise of discretionary power will assist the fiduciary to administer the trust or estate impartially, the fiduciary may:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-201(4)(a): 75A-5-203 exercise the power to adjust under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-201(4)(b): 75A-5-303 convert an income trust to a unitrust under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-201(4)(c): 75A-5-303 change the percentage or method used to calculate a unitrust amount under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-201(4)(d): 75A-5-303 convert a unitrust to an income trust under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-201(5): In making the determination under Subsection (4), the fiduciary shall consider the following factors:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-201(5)(a): the terms of the trust;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-201(5)(b): the nature, distribution standards, and expected duration of the trust;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-201(5)(c): the effect of the allocation rules, including specific adjustments between income and principal, under Part 4, Allocation of Receipts, Part 5, Allocation of Disbursements, Part 6, Death of Individual or Termination of Income Interest, and Part 7, Apportionment at Beginning and End of Income Interest;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-201(5)(d): the desirability of liquidity and regularity of income;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-201(5)(e): the desirability of the preservation and appreciation of principal;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-201(5)(f): the extent to which an asset is used or may be used by a beneficiary;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-201(5)(g): the increase or decrease in the value of principal assets, reasonably determined by the fiduciary;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-201(5)(h): whether and to what extent the terms of the trust:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-201(5)(h)(i): give the fiduciary power to accumulate income or invade principal; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-201(5)(h)(ii): prohibit the fiduciary from accumulating income or invading principal;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-201(5)(i): the extent to which the fiduciary has accumulated income or invaded principal in preceding accounting periods;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-201(5)(j): the effect of current and reasonably expected economic conditions; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-201(5)(k): the reasonably expected tax consequences of the exercise of the power.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-202(2): The court may not order a fiduciary to change a fiduciary decision, unless the court determines that the fiduciary decision was an abuse of the fiduciary's discretion.

Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-202(3)(b)(iii): the fiduciary to distribute an amount to a beneficiary;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-202(3)(b)(iv): a beneficiary to return some or all of a distribution; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-202(3)(b)(v): the fiduciary to withhold an amount from one or more future distributions to a beneficiary.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-202(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-202(4)(a): On petition by a fiduciary for instruction, the court may determine whether a proposed fiduciary decision will result in an abuse of the fiduciary's discretion.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-202(4)(b): A beneficiary that opposes the proposed decision has the burden to establish that the proposed decision will result in an abuse of the fiduciary's discretion if the petition:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-202(4)(b)(i): describes the proposed decision;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-202(4)(b)(ii): contains sufficient information to inform the beneficiary of the reasons for making the proposed decision and the facts on which the fiduciary relies; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-202(4)(b)(iii): explains how the beneficiary will be affected by the proposed decision.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-203 Fiduciary's power to adjust.
------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-203(1): Except as otherwise provided in the terms of a trust or this section, a fiduciary, in a record, without court approval, may adjust between income and principal if the fiduciary determines the exercise of the power to adjust will assist the fiduciary to administer the trust or estate impartially.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-203(2): This section does not create a duty to exercise or consider the power to adjust under Subsection (1) or to inform a beneficiary about the applicability of this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-203(3): A fiduciary that in good faith exercises or fails to exercise the power to adjust under Subsection (1) is not liable to a person affected by the exercise or failure to exercise.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-203(4): 75A-5-201; 75A-5-401; 75A-5-408; 75A-5-413 In deciding whether and to what extent to exercise the power to adjust under Subsection (1), a fiduciary shall consider all factors the fiduciary considers relevant, including the relevant factors in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-203(5): 75A-5-408 A fiduciary may not exercise the power to make an adjustment under Subsection (1) or the power to make a determination that an allocation is insubstantial under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-203(5)(a): the adjustment or determination would reduce the amount payable to a current income beneficiary from a trust that qualifies for a special tax benefit, except to the extent the adjustment is made to provide for a reasonable apportionment of the total return of the trust between the current income beneficiary and successor beneficiaries;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-203(5)(b): the adjustment or determination would change the amount payable to a beneficiary, as a fixed annuity or a fixed fraction of the value of the trust assets, under the terms of the trust;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-203(5)(c): the adjustment or determination would reduce an amount that is permanently set aside for a charitable purpose under the terms of the trust, unless both income and principal are set aside for the charitable purpose;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-203(5)(d): possessing or exercising the power would cause a person to be treated as the owner of all or part of the trust for federal income tax purposes;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-203(5)(e): possessing or exercising the power would cause all or part of the value of the trust assets to be included in the gross estate of an individual for federal estate tax purposes;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-203(5)(f): possessing or exercising the power would cause an individual to be treated as making a gift for federal gift tax purposes;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-203(5)(g): the fiduciary is not an independent person;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-203(5)(h): the trust is irrevocable and provides for income to be paid to the settlor and possessing or exercising the power would cause the adjusted principal or income to be considered an available resource or available income under a public-benefit program; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-203(5)(i): the trust is a unitrust under Part 3, Unitrust.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-203(6): If Subsection (5)(d), (e), (f), or (g) applies to a fiduciary:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-203(6)(a): a co-fiduciary to which Subsections (5)(d) through (g) do not apply may exercise the power to adjust, unless the exercise of the power to adjust by the remaining co-fiduciary or co-fiduciaries is not permitted by the terms of the trust or law other than this chapter; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-203(6)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-203(6)(b)(i): if there is no co-fiduciary to which Subsections (5)(d) through (g) do not apply:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-203(6)(b)(i)(A): except as otherwise provided in Subsection (6)(b)(ii)(A),  the fiduciary may appoint a co-fiduciary to which Subsections (5)(d) through (g) do not apply;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-203(6)(b)(i)(B): except as otherwise provided in Subsection (6)(b)(ii)(B), the appointed co-fiduciary may exercise the power to adjust under Subsection (1); and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-203(6)(b)(i)(C): the appointed co-fiduciary may be a special fiduciary with limited powers.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-203(6)(b)(ii): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-203(6)(b)(ii)(A): If the appointment of a co-fiduciary is not permitted by the terms of the trust or by a provision of law outside this chapter, a fiduciary may not appoint a co-fiduciary.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-203(6)(b)(ii)(B): If the exercise of the power to adjust by a co-fiduciary is not permitted by the terms of the trust or by a provision of law outside this chapter, the co-fiduciary may not exercise the power to adjust under Subsection (1).
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-203(7): A fiduciary may release or delegate to a co-fiduciary the power to adjust under Subsection (1) if the fiduciary determines that the fiduciary's possession or exercise of the power to adjust will or may:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-203(7)(a): cause a result described in Subsections (5)(a) through (f) or (h); or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-203(7)(b): deprive the trust of a tax benefit or impose a tax burden not described in Subsections (5)(a) through (f).
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-203(8): A fiduciary's release or delegation to a co-fiduciary under Subsection (7) of the power to adjust under Subsection (1):
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-203(8)(a): must be in a record;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-203(8)(b): applies to the entire power to adjust, unless the release or delegation provides a limitation, which may be a limitation to the power to adjust:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-203(8)(b)(i): from income to principal;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-203(8)(b)(ii): from principal to income;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-203(8)(b)(iii): for specified property; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-203(8)(b)(iv): in specified circumstances;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-203(8)(c): for a delegation, may be modified by a redelegation under this subsection by the co-fiduciary to which the delegation is made; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-203(8)(d): subject to Subsection (8)(c), is permanent, unless the release or delegation provides a specified period, including a period measured by the life of an individual or the lives of more than one individual.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-203(9): Terms of a trust that deny or limit the power to adjust between income and principal do not affect the application of this section, unless the terms of the trust expressly deny or limit the power to adjust under Subsection (1).
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-203(10): The exercise of the power to adjust under Subsection (1) in any accounting period may apply to the current accounting period, the immediately preceding accounting period, and one or more subsequent accounting periods.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-203(11): 75-7-811; 75-7-103 A description of the exercise of the power to adjust under Subsection (1) shall be:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-203(11)(a): 75-7-811 included in a report, if any, sent to beneficiaries under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-203(11)(b): 75-7-103 communicated at least annually to the qualified beneficiaries determined under Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-301 Definitions for part.
-----------------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-301(1): 75A-5-307 "Applicable value" means the amount of the net fair market value of a trust taken into account under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-301(2): "Express unitrust" means a trust for which, under the terms of the trust without regard to this part, income or net income is permitted or required to be calculated as a unitrust amount.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-301(3): "Income trust" means a trust that is not a unitrust.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-301(4): "Net fair market value of a trust" means the fair market value of the assets of the trust minus the noncontingent liabilities of the trust.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-301(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-301(5)(a): "Unitrust" means a trust for which net income is a unitrust amount.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-301(5)(b): "Unitrust" includes an express unitrust.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-301(6): "Unitrust amount" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-301(6)(a): an amount computed by multiplying a determined value of a trust by a determined percentage; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-301(6)(b): for a unitrust administered under a unitrust policy, the applicable value multiplied by the unitrust rate.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-301(7): 75A-5-305; 75A-5-309; 75A-5-303 "Unitrust policy" means a policy described in Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-301(8): "Unitrust rate" means the rate used to compute the unitrust amount under Subsection (6) for a unitrust administered under a unitrust policy.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-302 Application -- Duties and remedies.
-------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-302(1): Except as otherwise provided in Subsection (2), this part applies to:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-302(1)(a): an income trust, unless the terms of the trust expressly prohibit use of this part by:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-302(1)(a)(i): a specific reference to this part; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-302(1)(a)(ii): an explicit expression of intent that net income not be calculated as a unitrust amount; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-302(1)(b): an express unitrust, except to the extent the terms of the trust explicitly:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-302(1)(b)(i): prohibit use of this part by a specific reference to this part;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-302(1)(b)(ii): prohibit conversion to an income trust; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-302(1)(b)(iii): limit changes to the method of calculating the unitrust amount.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-302(2): This part does not apply to a trust described in Section 170(f)(2)(B), 642(c)(5), 664(d), 2702(a)(3)(A)(ii) or (iii), or 2702(b) of the Internal Revenue Code.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-302(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-302(3)(a): An income trust to which this part applies under Subsection (1)(a) may be converted to a unitrust under this part regardless of the terms of the trust concerning distributions.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-302(3)(b): Conversion to a unitrust under this part does not affect other terms of the trust concerning distributions of income or principal.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-302(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-302(4)(a): This part applies to an estate only to the extent a trust is a beneficiary of the estate.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-302(4)(b): To the extent of the trust's interest in the estate, and in the same manner as for a trust under this part:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-302(4)(b)(i): the estate may be administered as a unitrust;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-302(4)(b)(ii): the administration of the estate as a unitrust may be discontinued; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-302(4)(b)(iii): the percentage or method used to calculate the unitrust amount may be changed.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-302(5): This part does not create a duty to take or consider action under this part or to inform a beneficiary about the applicability of this part.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-302(6): A fiduciary that in good faith takes or fails to take an action under this part is not liable to a person affected by the action or inaction of the fiduciary.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-303 Authority of fiduciary.
-------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-303(1): A fiduciary, without court approval, by complying with Subsections (2) and (6), may:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-303(1)(a): convert an income trust to a unitrust if the fiduciary adopts, in a record, a unitrust policy for the trust providing:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-303(1)(a)(i): that, in administering the trust, the net income of the trust will be a unitrust amount rather than net income determined without regard to this part; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-303(1)(a)(ii): the percentage and method used to calculate the unitrust amount;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-303(1)(b): change the percentage or method used to calculate a unitrust amount for a unitrust if the fiduciary adopts in a record a unitrust policy or an amendment or replacement of a unitrust policy providing changes in the percentage or method used to calculate the unitrust amount; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-303(1)(c): convert a unitrust to an income trust if the fiduciary adopts, in a record, a determination that, in administering the trust, the net income of the trust will be net income determined without regard to this part rather than a unitrust amount.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-303(2): 75A-5-304; 75-7-103; 75A-5-304; 75A-5-304 A fiduciary may take an action under Subsection (1) if:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-303(2)(a): the fiduciary determines that the action will assist the fiduciary to administer a trust impartially;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-303(2)(b): 75A-5-304 the fiduciary sends a notice in a record, in the manner required by Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-303(2)(c): the fiduciary sends a copy of the notice under Subsection (2)(b) to each settlor of the trust which is:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-303(2)(c)(i): if an individual, living; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-303(2)(c)(ii): if not an individual, in existence;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-303(2)(d): 75-7-103; 75A-5-304 at least one member of each class of the qualified beneficiaries determined under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-303(2)(d)(i): if an individual, legally competent;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-303(2)(d)(ii): if not an individual, in existence; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-303(2)(d)(iii): 75A-5-304 represented in the manner provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-303(2)(e): 75A-5-304 the fiduciary does not receive, by the date specified in the notice under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-303(3): 75A-5-304; 75A-5-304; 75A-5-304; 75A-5-304; 75A-5-304
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-303(3)(a): 75A-5-304; 75A-5-304 If a fiduciary receives, not later than the date stated in the notice under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-303(3)(a)(i): require the fiduciary to take the proposed action;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-303(3)(a)(ii): require the fiduciary to take the proposed action with modifications; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-303(3)(a)(iii): prevent the proposed action.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-303(3)(b): 75A-5-304; 75A-5-304; 75A-5-304 A person described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-303(3)(b)(i): 75A-5-304 consented under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-303(3)(b)(ii): 75A-5-304 objected under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-303(4): 75A-5-304 If, after sending a notice under Subsection (2)(b), a fiduciary decides not to take the action proposed in the notice, the fiduciary shall notify each person described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-303(5): If a beneficiary requests in a record that a fiduciary take an action described in Subsection (1) and the fiduciary declines to act or does not act within 90 days after receiving the request, the beneficiary may request the court to direct the fiduciary to take the action requested.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-303(6): 75A-5-201 In deciding whether and how to take an action authorized by Subsection (1), or whether and how to respond to a request by a beneficiary under Subsection (5), a fiduciary shall consider all factors relevant to the trust and the beneficiaries, including the relevant factors in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-303(7): 75A-5-203; 75A-5-203 For a reason described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-303(7)(a): release or delegate the power to convert an income trust to a unitrust under Subsection (1)(a);
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-303(7)(b): change the percentage or method used to calculate a unitrust amount under Subsection (1)(b); or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-303(7)(c): convert a unitrust to an income trust under Subsection (1)(c).

Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-304(2): 75-7-301; 75-7-305 The representation provisions of Sections

Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-304(3)(a): 75A-5-303 A person may consent in a record at any time to action proposed under Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-306 Unitrust rate.
----------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-306(1): 75A-5-309 Except as otherwise provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-306(1)(a): a fixed unitrust rate; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-306(1)(b): a unitrust rate that is determined for each period using:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-306(1)(b)(i): a market index or other published data; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-306(1)(b)(ii): a mathematical blend of market indices or other published data over a stated number of preceding periods.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-306(2): 75A-5-309 Except as otherwise provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-306(2)(a): a limit on how high the unitrust rate determined under Subsection (1)(b) may rise;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-306(2)(b): a limit on how low the unitrust rate determined under Subsection (1)(b) may fall;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-306(2)(c): a limit on how much the unitrust rate determined under Subsection (1)(b) may increase over the unitrust rate for the preceding period or a mathematical blend of unitrust rates over a stated number of preceding periods;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-306(2)(d): a limit on how much the unitrust rate determined under Subsection (1)(b) may decrease below the unitrust rate for the preceding period or a mathematical blend of unitrust rates over a stated number of preceding periods; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-306(2)(e): a mathematical blend of any of the unitrust rates determined under Subsection (1)(b) and Subsections (2)(a) through (d).


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-307 Applicable value.
-------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-307(1): A unitrust policy shall provide the method for determining the fair market value of an asset for the purpose of determining the unitrust amount, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-307(1)(a): the frequency of valuing the asset, which need not require a valuation in every period; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-307(1)(b): the date for valuing the asset in each period that the asset is valued.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-307(2): 75A-5-309 Except as otherwise provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-307(2)(a): obtaining an appraisal of an asset for which fair market value is not readily available;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-307(2)(b): exclusion of specific assets or groups or types of assets;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-307(2)(c): other exceptions or modifications of the treatment of specific assets or groups or types of assets;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-307(2)(d): identification and treatment of cash or property held for distribution;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-307(2)(e): use of:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-307(2)(e)(i): an average of fair market values over a stated number of preceding periods; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-307(2)(e)(ii): another mathematical blend of fair market values over a stated number of preceding periods;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-307(2)(f): a limit on how much the applicable value of all assets, groups of assets, or individual assets may increase over:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-307(2)(f)(i): the corresponding applicable value for the preceding period; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-307(2)(f)(ii): a mathematical blend of applicable values over a stated number of preceding time periods;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-307(2)(g): a limit on how much the applicable value of all assets, groups of assets, or individual assets may decrease below:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-307(2)(g)(i): the corresponding applicable value for the preceding period; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-307(2)(g)(ii): a mathematical blend of applicable values over a stated number of preceding periods;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-307(2)(h): the treatment of accrued income and other features of an asset that affect value; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-307(2)(i): determining the liabilities of the trust, including treatment of liabilities to conform with the treatment of assets under Subsections (2)(a) through (h).

---------------------------------------

Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-309 Special tax benefits -- Other rules.
--------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-309(1): A unitrust policy may:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-309(1)(a): provide methods and standards for:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-309(1)(a)(i): determining the timing of distributions;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-309(1)(a)(ii): making distributions in cash or in kind or partly in cash and partly in kind; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-309(1)(a)(iii): correcting an underpayment or overpayment to a beneficiary based on the unitrust amount if there is an error in calculating the unitrust amount;

Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-401 Receipts from entity -- Character of receipts from entity.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-401(1): 75A-5-402; 75A-5-403; 75A-5-416 As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-401(1)(a): "Capital distribution" means an entity distribution of money that is a:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-401(1)(a)(i): return of capital; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-401(1)(a)(ii): distribution in total or partial liquidation of the entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-401(1)(b): 75A-5-402; 75A-5-403; 75A-5-416
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-401(1)(b)(i): "Entity" means a corporation, partnership, limited liability company, regulated investment company, real estate investment trust, common trust fund, or any other organization or arrangement in which a fiduciary owns or holds an interest, regardless of whether the entity is a taxpayer for federal income tax purposes.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-401(1)(b)(ii): 75A-5-402; 75A-5-403; 75A-5-416 "Entity" does not include:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-401(1)(b)(ii)(A): 75A-5-402 a trust or estate to which Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-401(1)(b)(ii)(B): 75A-5-403 a business or other activity to which Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-401(1)(b)(ii)(C): an asset-backed security; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-401(1)(b)(ii)(D): 75A-5-416 an instrument or arrangement to which Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-401(1)(c): "Entity distribution" means a payment or transfer by an entity made to a person in the person's capacity as an owner or holder of an interest in the entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-401(2): In this section, an attribute or action of an entity includes an attribute or action of any other entity in which the entity owns or holds an interest, including an interest owned or held indirectly through another entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-401(3): Except as otherwise provided in Subsections (4)(b) through (d), a fiduciary shall allocate to income:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-401(3)(a): money received in an entity distribution; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-401(3)(b): tangible personal property of nominal value received from the entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-401(4): A fiduciary shall allocate to principal:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-401(4)(a): property received in an entity distribution that is not:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-401(4)(a)(i): money; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-401(4)(a)(ii): tangible personal property of nominal value;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-401(4)(b): money received in an entity distribution in an exchange for part or all of the fiduciary's interest in the entity, to the extent the entity distribution reduces the fiduciary's interest in the entity relative to the interests of other persons that own or hold interests in the entity;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-401(4)(c): money received in an entity distribution that the fiduciary determines or estimates is a capital distribution; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-401(4)(d): money received in an entity distribution from an entity that is:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-401(4)(d)(i): a regulated investment company or real estate investment trust if the money received is a capital gain dividend for federal income tax purposes; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-401(4)(d)(ii): treated for federal income tax purposes in a comparable manner to the treatment described in Subsection (4)(d)(i).
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-401(5): A fiduciary may determine or estimate that money received in an entity distribution is a capital distribution:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-401(5)(a): by relying without inquiry or investigation on a characterization of the entity distribution provided by or on behalf of the entity, unless the fiduciary:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-401(5)(a)(i): determines, on the basis of information known to the fiduciary, that the characterization is or may be incorrect; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-401(5)(a)(ii): owns or holds more than 50% of the voting interest in the entity;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-401(5)(b): by determining or estimating, on the basis of information known to the fiduciary or provided to the fiduciary by or on behalf of the entity, that the total amount of money and property received by the fiduciary in the entity distribution or a series of related entity distributions is or will be greater than 20% of the fair market value of the fiduciary's interest in the entity; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-401(5)(c): if neither Subsection (5)(a) nor (b) applies, by considering the factors in Subsection (6) and the information known to the fiduciary or provided to the fiduciary by or on behalf of the entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-401(6): 75A-5-407; 75A-5-410; 75A-5-411; 75A-5-412 In making a determination or estimate under Subsection (5)(c), a fiduciary may consider:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-401(6)(a): a characterization of an entity distribution provided by or on behalf of the entity;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-401(6)(b): the amount of money or property received in:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-401(6)(b)(i): the entity distribution; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-401(6)(b)(ii): what the fiduciary determines is or will be a series of related entity distributions;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-401(6)(c): 75A-5-407; 75A-5-410; 75A-5-411; 75A-5-412 the amount described in Subsection (6)(b) compared to the amount that the fiduciary determines or estimates is, during the current or preceding accounting periods:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-401(6)(c)(i): the entity's operating income;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-401(6)(c)(ii): the proceeds of the entity's sale or other disposition of:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-401(6)(c)(ii)(A): all or part of the business or other activity conducted by the entity;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-401(6)(c)(ii)(B): one or more business assets that are not sold to customers in the ordinary course of the business or other activity conducted by the entity; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-401(6)(c)(ii)(C): one or more assets other than business assets, unless the entity's primary activity is to invest in assets to realize gain on the disposition of all or some of the assets;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-401(6)(c)(iii): if the entity's primary activity is to invest in assets to realize gain on the disposition of all or some of the assets, the gain realized on the disposition;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-401(6)(c)(iv): the entity's regular, periodic entity distributions;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-401(6)(c)(v): the amount of money that the entity has accumulated;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-401(6)(c)(vi): the amount of money that the entity has borrowed;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-401(6)(c)(vii): 75A-5-407; 75A-5-410; 75A-5-411; 75A-5-412 the amount of money that the entity has received from the sources described in Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-401(6)(c)(viii): the amount of money that the entity has received from a source not otherwise described in this subsection; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-401(6)(d): any other factor the fiduciary determines is relevant.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-401(7): If, after applying Subsections (3) through (6), a fiduciary determines that a part of an entity distribution is a capital distribution but the fiduciary is in doubt about the amount of the entity distribution that is a capital distribution, the fiduciary shall allocate to principal the amount of the entity distribution that is in doubt.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-401(8): If a fiduciary receives additional information about the application of this section to an entity distribution before the fiduciary has paid part of the entity distribution to a beneficiary, the fiduciary may consider the additional information before making the payment to the beneficiary and may change a decision to make the payment to the beneficiary.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-401(9): 75A-5-203 If a fiduciary receives additional information about the application of this section to an entity distribution after the fiduciary has paid part of the entity distribution to a beneficiary, the fiduciary is not required to change or recover the payment to the beneficiary but may consider that information in determining whether to exercise the power to adjust under Section
