Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-602(3): To the extent that a fiduciary does not distribute under this section all the collected but undistributed net income to each beneficiary on or before a distribution date, the fiduciary shall maintain records showing the interest of each beneficiary in the net income.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-602(4): If this section applies to income from an asset, a fiduciary may apply Subsection (2) to net gain or loss realized from the disposition of the asset after the decedent's death, an income interest's terminating event, or the preceding distribution by the fiduciary.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-701 When right to income begins and ends.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-701(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-701(1)(a): An income beneficiary is entitled to net income in accordance with the terms of the trust from the date on which an income interest begins.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-701(1)(b): The income interest begins on the date that is specified in the terms of the trust or, if no date is specified, on the date an asset becomes subject to:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-701(1)(b)(i): the trust for the current income beneficiary; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-701(1)(b)(ii): a successive interest for a successor beneficiary.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-701(2): An asset becomes subject to a trust under Subsection (1)(b)(i):
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-701(2)(a): for an asset that is transferred to the trust during the settlor's life, on the date the asset is transferred;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-701(2)(b): for an asset that becomes subject to the trust because of a decedent's death, on the date of the decedent's death, even if there is an intervening period of administration of the decedent's estate; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-701(2)(c): for an asset that is transferred to a fiduciary by a third party because of a decedent's death, on the date of the decedent's death.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-701(3): An asset becomes subject to a successive interest under Subsection (1)(b)(ii) on the day after the preceding income interest ends, as determined under Subsection (4), even if there is an intervening period of administration to wind up the preceding income interest.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-701(4): An income interest ends on the day before an income beneficiary dies or another terminating event occurs or on the last day of a period during which there is no beneficiary to which a fiduciary is permitted or required to  distribute income.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-702 Apportionment of receipts and disbursements when decedent dies or income interest begins.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-702(1): 75A-5-601 A fiduciary shall allocate an income receipt or disbursement, other than a receipt to which Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-702(1)(a): for an estate, the decedent died; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-702(1)(b): for a trust or successive interest, an income interest begins.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-702(2): If the due date of a periodic income receipt or disbursement occurs on or after the date on which a decedent died or an income interest begins, a fiduciary shall allocate the receipt or disbursement to income.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-702(3): If an income receipt or disbursement is not periodic or has no due date, a fiduciary shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-702(3)(a): treat the receipt or disbursement under this section as accruing from day to day; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-702(3)(b): allocate:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-702(3)(b)(i): to principal, the portion of the receipt or disbursement accruing before the date on which a decedent died or an income interest begins; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-702(3)(b)(ii): to income, the balance.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-702(4): A receipt or disbursement is periodic under Subsections (2) and (3) if:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-702(4)(a): the receipt or disbursement shall be paid at regular intervals under an obligation to make payments; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-702(4)(b): the payor customarily makes payments at regular intervals.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-702(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-702(5)(a): An item of income or obligation is due under this section on the date on which the payor is required to make a payment.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-702(5)(b): If a payment date is not stated, there is no due date.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-702(6): 75A-5-401 Distributions to shareholders or other owners from an entity to which Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-702(6)(a): on the date fixed by or on behalf of the entity for determining the persons entitled to receive the distribution;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-702(6)(b): if no date is fixed, on the date of the decision by or on behalf of the entity to make the distribution; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-702(6)(c): if no date is fixed and the fiduciary does not know the date of the decision by or on behalf of the entity to make the distribution, on the date the fiduciary learns of the decision.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-703 Apportionment when income interest ends.
------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-703(1): As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-703(1)(a): "Undistributed income" means net income received on or before the date on which an income interest ends.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-703(1)(b): "Undistributed income" does not include an item of income or expense that is due or accrued or net income that has been added or is required to be added, to principal under the terms of the trust.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-703(2): Except as otherwise provided in Subsection (3), when a mandatory income interest of a beneficiary ends, the fiduciary shall pay the beneficiary's share of the undistributed income that is not disposed of under the terms of the trust to the beneficiary or, if the beneficiary does not survive the date that the interest ends, to the beneficiary's estate.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-703(3): If a beneficiary has an unqualified power to withdraw more than 5% of the value of a trust immediately before an income interest ends:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-703(3)(a): the fiduciary shall allocate to principal the undistributed income from the portion of the trust that may be withdrawn; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-703(3)(b): Subsection (2) applies only to the balance of the undistributed income.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-703(4): When a fiduciary's obligation to pay a fixed annuity or a fixed fraction of the value of assets ends, the fiduciary shall prorate the final payment as required to preserve an income tax, gift tax, estate tax, or other tax benefit.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-801 Uniformity of application and construction.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------
In applying and construing this uniform act, consideration must be given to the need to promote uniformity of the law with respect to the uniform act's subject matter among states that enact this uniform law.

Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-802 Relation to Electronic Signatures in Global and National Commerce Act.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
This chapter modifies, limits, or supersedes the Electronic Signatures in Global and National Commerce Act, 15 U.S.C. Sec. 7001 et seq., but does not modify, limit, or supersede Section 101(c) of that act, 15 U.S.C. Sec. 7001(c), or authorize electronic delivery of any of the notices described in Section 103(b) of that act, 15 U.S.C. Sec. 7003(b).

Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-803 Application to trust or estate.
---------------------------------------------------------------
This chapter applies to a trust or estate existing or created on or after July 1, 2020, except as otherwise expressly provided in the terms of the trust or this chapter.

Utah Code Annotated § 75A-5-804 Severability.
---------------------------------------------
If any provision of this chapter or the application of this chapter to any person or circumstance is held invalid, the invalidity does not affect other provisions or applications of this chapter that can be given effect without the invalid provision or application, and to this end the provisions of this chapter are severable.

Utah Code Annotated - Title 75A - Chapter 6 - Uniform Fiduciary Access to Digital Assets Act
********************************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-101 Reserved.
-----------------------------------------
Reserved.

Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-102 Definitions for chapter.
--------------------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-102(1): "Account" means an arrangement under a terms of service agreement in which a custodian carries, maintains, processes, receives, or stores a digital asset of the user or provides goods or services to the user.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-102(2): "Agent" means an attorney in fact granted authority under a durable or nondurable power of attorney.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-102(3): "Carries" means engages in the transmission of an electronic communication.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-102(4): "Catalogue of electronic communications" means information that identifies each person with which a user has had an electronic communication, the time and date of the communication, and the electronic address of the person.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-102(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-102(5)(a): "Conservator" means a person appointed by a court to manage the estate of a living individual.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-102(5)(b): "Conservator" includes a limited conservator.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-102(6): "Content of an electronic communication" means information concerning the substance or meaning of the communication that:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-102(6)(a): has been sent or received by a user;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-102(6)(b): is in electronic storage by a custodian providing an electronic communication service to the public or is carried or maintained by a custodian providing a remote computing service to the public; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-102(6)(c): is not readily accessible to the public.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-102(7): "Court" means a court with jurisdiction under Title 78A, Judiciary and Judicial Administration.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-102(8): "Custodian" means a person that carries, maintains, processes, receives, or stores a digital asset of a user.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-102(9): "Designated recipient" means a person chosen by a user using an online tool to administer digital assets of the user.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-102(10): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-102(10)(a): "Digital asset" means an electronic record in which an individual has a right or interest.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-102(10)(b): "Digital asset" does not include an underlying asset or liability unless the asset or liability is itself an electronic record.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-102(11): "Electronic" means relating to technology having electrical, digital, magnetic, wireless, optical, electromagnetic, or similar capabilities.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-102(12): "Electronic communication" has the same meaning as the definition in 18 U.S.C. Sec. 2510(12).
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-102(13): "Electronic communication service" means a custodian that provides to a user the ability to send or receive an electronic communication.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-102(14): 75-1-201 "Estate" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-102(15): "Fiduciary" means an original, additional, or successor personal representative, conservator, guardian, agent, or trustee.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-102(16): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-102(16)(a): "Guardian" means a person appointed by a court to manage the affairs of a living individual.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-102(16)(b): "Guardian" includes a limited guardian.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-102(17): "Information" means data, text, images, videos, sounds, codes, computer programs, software, databases, or the like.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-102(18): "Online tool" means an electronic service provided by a custodian that allows the user, in an agreement distinct from the terms of service agreement between the custodian and user, to provide directions for disclosure or nondisclosure of digital assets to a third person.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-102(19): "Person" means an individual, estate, business or nonprofit entity, public corporation, government or governmental subdivision, agency, instrumentality, or other legal entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-102(20): 75-1-201 "Personal representative" means an executor, administrator, special administrator as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-102(21): "Power of attorney" means a record that grants an agent authority to act in the place of a principal.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-102(22): "Principal" means an individual who grants authority to an agent in a power of attorney.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-102(23): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-102(23)(a): "Protected person" means an individual for whom a conservator or guardian has been appointed.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-102(23)(b): "Protected person" includes an individual for whom an application for the appointment of a conservator or guardian is pending.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-102(24): "Record" means information that is inscribed on a tangible medium or that is stored in an electronic or other medium and is retrievable in perceivable form.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-102(25): "Remote computing service" means a custodian that provides to a user computer processing services or the storage of digital assets by means of an electronic communications system, as defined in 18 U.S.C. Sec. 2510(14).
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-102(26): 75-1-201 "Successor personal representative" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-102(27): "Terms of service agreement" means an agreement that controls the relationship between a user and a custodian.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-102(28): 75-1-201 "Trust" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-102(29): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-102(29)(a): "Trustee" means a fiduciary with legal title to property pursuant to an agreement or declaration that creates a beneficial interest in another.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-102(29)(b): "Trustee" includes a successor trustee.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-102(30): "User" means a person that has an account with a custodian.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-102(31): "Will" includes a codicil, a testamentary instrument that only appoints an executor, and an instrument that revokes or revises a testamentary instrument.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-103 Applicability.
----------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-103(1): This chapter applies to:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-103(1)(a): a fiduciary or agent acting under a will or power of attorney executed before, on, or after May 9, 2017;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-103(1)(b): a personal representative acting for a decedent who died before, on, or after May 9, 2017;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-103(1)(c): a conservatorship or guardianship proceeding commenced before, on, or after May 9, 2017; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-103(1)(d): a trustee acting under a trust created before, on, or after May 9, 2017.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-103(2): This chapter applies to a custodian if the user resides in this state or resided in this state at the time of the user's death.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-103(3): This chapter does not apply to a digital asset of an employer used by an employee in the ordinary course of the employer's business.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-104 User direction for disclosure of digital assets.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-104(1): A user may use an online tool to direct the custodian to disclose or not to disclose to a designated recipient some or all of the user's digital assets, including the content of electronic communications. If the online tool allows the user to modify or delete a direction at all times, a direction regarding disclosure using an online tool overrides a contrary direction by the user in a will, trust, power of attorney, or other record.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-104(2): If a user has not used an online tool to give direction under Subsection (1) or if the custodian has not provided an online tool, the user may allow or prohibit in a will, trust, power of attorney, or other record disclosure to a fiduciary of some or all of the user's digital assets, including the content of electronic communications sent or received by the user.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-104(3): A user's direction under Subsection (1) or (2) overrides a contrary provision in a terms of service agreement that does not require the user to act affirmatively and distinctly from the user's assent to the terms of service.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-105 Terms of service agreement.
-----------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-105(1): This chapter does not change or impair a right of a custodian or a user under a terms of service agreement to access and use digital assets of the user.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-105(2): This chapter does not give a fiduciary or designated recipient any new or expanded rights other than those held by the user for whom, or for whose estate, the fiduciary or designated recipient acts or represents.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-105(3): 75A-6-104 A fiduciary's or designated recipient's access to digital assets may be modified or eliminated by a user, by federal law, or by a terms of service agreement if the user has not provided direction under Section


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-106 Procedure for disclosing digital assets.
------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-106(1): When disclosing digital assets of a user under this chapter, the custodian may at the custodian's sole discretion:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-106(1)(a): grant a fiduciary or designated recipient full access to the user's account;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-106(1)(b): grant a fiduciary or designated recipient partial access to the user's account sufficient to perform the tasks with which the fiduciary or designated recipient is charged; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-106(1)(c): provide a fiduciary or designated recipient a copy in a record of any digital asset that, on the date the custodian received the request for disclosure, the user could have accessed if the user were alive and had full capacity and access to the account.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-106(2): A custodian may assess a reasonable administrative charge for the cost of disclosing digital assets under this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-106(3): A custodian need not disclose under this chapter a digital asset deleted by a user.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-106(4): If a user directs or a fiduciary requests a custodian to disclose under this chapter some, but not all, of the user's digital assets, the custodian need not disclose the assets if segregation of the assets would impose an undue burden on the custodian. If the custodian believes the direction or request imposes an undue burden, the custodian or fiduciary may seek an order from the court to disclose:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-106(4)(a): a subset limited by date of the user's digital assets;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-106(4)(b): all of the user's digital assets to the fiduciary or designated recipient;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-106(4)(c): none of the user's digital assets; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-106(4)(d): all of the user's digital assets to the court for review in camera.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-107 Disclosure of content of electronic communications of deceased user.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
If a deceased user consented to or a court directs disclosure of the contents of electronic communications of the user, the custodian shall disclose to the personal representative of the estate of the user the content of an electronic communication sent or received by the user if the representative gives the custodian:Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-107(1): a written request for disclosure in physical or electronic form;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-107(2): a certified copy of the death certificate of the user;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-107(3): a certified copy of the letter of appointment of the representative or a small estate affidavit or court order;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-107(4): unless the user provided direction using an online tool, a copy of the user's will, trust, power of attorney, or other record evidencing the user's consent to disclosure of the content of electronic communications; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-107(5): if requested by the custodian:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-107(5)(a): a number, username, address, or other unique subscriber or account identifier assigned by the custodian to identify the user's account;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-107(5)(b): evidence linking the account to the user; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-107(5)(c): a finding by the court that:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-107(5)(c)(i): the user had a specific account with the custodian, identifiable by the information specified in Subsection (5)(a);
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-107(5)(c)(ii): disclosure of the content of electronic communications of the user would not violate 18 U.S.C. Sec. 2701 et seq., 47 U.S.C. Sec. 222, or other applicable law;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-107(5)(c)(iii): unless the user provided direction using an online tool, the user consented to disclosure of the content of electronic communications; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-107(5)(c)(iv): disclosure of the content of electronic communications of the user is reasonably necessary for administration of the estate.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-108 Disclosure of other digital assets of deceased user.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Unless the user prohibited disclosure of digital assets or the court directs otherwise, a custodian shall disclose to the personal representative of the estate of a deceased user a catalogue of electronic communications sent or received by the user and digital assets, other than the content of electronic communications, of the user, if the representative gives the custodian:Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-108(1): a written request for disclosure in physical or electronic form;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-108(2): a certified copy of the death certificate of the user;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-108(3): a certified copy of the letter of appointment of the representative, a small estate affidavit, or court order; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-108(4): if requested by the custodian:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-108(4)(a): a number, username, address, or other unique subscriber or account identifier assigned by the custodian to identify the user's account;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-108(4)(b): evidence linking the account to the user;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-108(4)(c): an affidavit stating that disclosure of the user's digital assets is reasonably necessary for administration of the estate; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-108(4)(d): a finding by the court that:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-108(4)(d)(i): the user had a specific account with the custodian, identifiable by the information specified in Subsection (4)(a); or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-108(4)(d)(ii): disclosure of the user's digital assets is reasonably necessary for administration of the estate.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-109 Disclosure of content of electronic communications of principal.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
To the extent a power of attorney expressly grants an agent authority over the content of electronic communications sent or received by the principal and unless directed otherwise by the principal or the court, a custodian shall disclose to the agent the content if the agent gives the custodian:Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-109(1): a written request for disclosure in physical or electronic form;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-109(2): an original or copy of the power of attorney expressly granting the agent authority over the content of electronic communications of the principal;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-109(3): a certification by the agent, under penalty of perjury, that the power of attorney is in effect; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-109(4): if requested by the custodian:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-109(4)(a): a number, username, address, or other unique subscriber or account identifier assigned by the custodian to identify the principal's account; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-109(4)(b): evidence linking the account to the principal.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-110 Disclosure of other digital assets of principal.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Unless otherwise ordered by the court, directed by the principal, or provided by a power of attorney, a custodian shall disclose to an agent with specific authority over digital assets, or general authority to act on behalf of a principal, a catalogue of electronic communications sent or received by the principal and digital assets, other than the content of electronic communications, of the principal if the agent gives the custodian:Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-110(1): a written request for disclosure in physical or electronic form;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-110(2): an original or a copy of the power of attorney that gives the agent specific authority over digital assets or general authority to act on behalf of the principal;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-110(3): a certification by the agent, under penalty of perjury, that the power of attorney is in effect; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-110(4): if requested by the custodian:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-110(4)(a): a number, username, address, or other unique subscriber or account identifier assigned by the custodian to identify the principal's account; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-110(4)(b): evidence linking the account to the principal.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-111 Disclosure of digital assets held in trust when trustee is original user.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Unless otherwise ordered by the court or provided in a trust, a custodian shall disclose to a trustee that is an original user of an account any digital asset of the account held in trust, including a catalogue of electronic communications of the trustee and the content of electronic communications.

Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-112 Disclosure of contents of electronic communications held in trust when trustee not original user.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Unless otherwise ordered by the court, directed by the user, or provided in a trust, a custodian shall disclose to a trustee that is not an original user of an account the content of an electronic communication sent or received by an original or successor user and carried, maintained, processed, received, or stored by the custodian in the account of the trust if the trustee gives the custodian:Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-112(1): a written request for disclosure in physical or electronic form;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-112(2): 75-7-1013 a certified copy of the trust instrument or a certification of the trust under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-112(3): a certification by the trustee, under penalty of perjury, that the trust exists and the trustee is a currently acting trustee of the trust; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-112(4): if requested by the custodian:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-112(4)(a): a number, username, address, or other unique subscriber or account identifier assigned by the custodian to identify the trust's account; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-112(4)(b): evidence linking the account to the trust.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-113 Disclosure of other digital assets held in trust when trustee not original user.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Unless otherwise ordered by the court, directed by the user, or provided in a trust, a custodian shall disclose, to a trustee that is not an original user of an account, a catalogue of electronic communications sent or received by an original or successor user and stored, carried, or maintained by the custodian in an account of the trust and any digital assets, other than the content of electronic communications, in which the trust has a right or interest if the trustee gives the custodian:Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-113(1): a written request for disclosure in physical or electronic form;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-113(2): 75-7-1013 a certified copy of the trust instrument or a certification of the trust under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-113(3): a certification by the trustee, under penalty of perjury, that the trust exists and the trustee is a currently acting trustee of the trust; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-113(4): if requested by the custodian:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-113(4)(a): a number, username, address, or other unique subscriber or account identifier assigned by the custodian to identify the trust's account; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-113(4)(b): evidence linking the account to the trust.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-114 Disclosure of digital assets to conservator or guardian of protected person.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-114(1): After an opportunity for a hearing under Chapter 5, Protection of Persons Under Disability and Their Property, the court may grant a conservator or guardian access to the digital assets of a protected person.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-114(2): Unless otherwise ordered by the court or directed by the user, a custodian shall disclose to a conservator or guardian the catalogue of electronic communications sent or received by a protected person and any digital assets, other than the content of electronic communications, in which the protected person has a right or interest if the conservator or guardian gives the custodian:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-114(2)(a): a written request for disclosure in physical or electronic form;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-114(2)(b): a certified copy of the court order that gives the conservator or guardian authority over the digital assets of the protected person; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-114(2)(c): if requested by the custodian:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-114(2)(c)(i): a number, username, address, or other unique subscriber or account identifier assigned by the custodian to identify the account of the protected person; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-114(2)(c)(ii): evidence linking the account to the protected person.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-114(3): A conservator or guardian with general authority to manage the assets of a protected person may request a custodian of the digital assets of the protected person to suspend or terminate an account of the protected person for good cause. A request made under this section must be accompanied by a certified copy of the court order giving the conservator or guardian authority over the protected person's property.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-115 Fiduciary duty and authority.
-------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-115(1): The legal duties imposed on a fiduciary charged with managing tangible property apply to the management of digital assets, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-115(1)(a): the duty of care;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-115(1)(b): the duty of loyalty; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-115(1)(c): the duty of confidentiality.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-115(2): 75A-6-104 A fiduciary's or designated recipient's authority with respect to a digital asset of a user:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-115(2)(a): 75A-6-104 except as otherwise provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-115(2)(b): is subject to other applicable law, including copyright law;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-115(2)(c): in the case of a fiduciary, is limited by the scope of the fiduciary's duties; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-115(2)(d): may not be used to impersonate the user.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-115(3): A fiduciary with authority over the property of a decedent, protected person, principal, or settlor has the right to access any digital asset in which the decedent, protected person, principal, or settlor had a right or interest and that is not held by a custodian or subject to a terms of service agreement.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-115(4): A fiduciary acting within the scope of the fiduciary's duties is an authorized user of the property of the decedent, protected person, principal, or settlor for the purpose of applicable computer fraud and unauthorized computer access laws.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-115(5): A fiduciary with authority over the tangible, personal property of a decedent, protected person, principal, or settlor:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-115(5)(a): has the right to access the property and any digital asset stored in it; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-115(5)(b): is an authorized user for the purpose of computer fraud and unauthorized computer access laws.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-115(6): A custodian may disclose information in an account to a fiduciary of the user when the information is required to terminate an account used to access digital assets licensed to the user.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-115(7): A fiduciary of a user may request a custodian to terminate the user's account. A request for termination shall be in writing, in either physical or electronic form, and accompanied by:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-115(7)(a): if the user is deceased, a certified copy of the death certificate of the user;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-115(7)(b): a certified copy of the letter of appointment of the representative, a small estate affidavit, or court order, power of attorney, or trust giving the fiduciary authority over the account; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-115(7)(c): if requested by the custodian:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-115(7)(c)(i): a number, username, address, or other unique subscriber or account identifier assigned by the custodian to identify the user's account;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-115(7)(c)(ii): evidence linking the account to the user; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-115(7)(c)(iii): a finding by the court that the user had a specific account with the custodian, identifiable by the information specified in Subsection (7)(c)(i).


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-116 Custodian compliance and immunity.
------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-116(1): 75A-6-107; 75A-6-115 Not later than 60 days after receipt of the information required under Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-116(2): An order under Subsection (1) directing compliance shall contain a finding that compliance is not in violation of 18 U.S.C. Sec. 2702.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-116(3): A custodian may notify the user that a request for disclosure or to terminate an account was made under this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-116(4): A custodian may deny a request under this chapter from a fiduciary or designated recipient for disclosure of digital assets or to terminate an account if the custodian is aware of any lawful access to the account following the receipt of the fiduciary's request.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-116(5): This chapter does not limit a custodian's ability to obtain or require a fiduciary or designated recipient requesting disclosure or termination under this chapter to obtain a court order that:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-116(5)(a): specifies that an account belongs to the protected person or principal;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-116(5)(b): specifies that there is sufficient consent from the protected person or principal to support the requested disclosure; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-116(5)(c): contains a finding required by law other than this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-116(6): A custodian and its officers, employees, and agents are immune from liability for an act or omission done in good faith in compliance with this chapter.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-117 Uniformity of application and construction.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------
In applying and construing this uniform act, consideration shall be given to the need to promote uniformity of the law with respect to its subject matter among states that enact this uniform law.

Utah Code Annotated § 75A-6-118 Relation to Electronic Signatures in Global and National Commerce Act.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
This chapter modifies, limits, or supersedes the Electronic Signatures in Global and National Commerce Act, 15 U.S.C. Sec. 7001 et seq., but does not modify, limit, or supersede Section 101(c) of that act or 15 U.S.C. Sec. 7001(c), or authorize electronic delivery of any of the notices described in Section 103(b) of that act or 15 U.S.C. Sec. 7003(b).

Utah Code Annotated - Title 75A - Chapter 7 - Uniform Act for Simplification of Fiduciary Security Transfers
************************************************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 75A-7-101 Reserved.
-----------------------------------------
Reserved.

Utah Code Annotated § 75A-7-102 Definitions for chapter.
--------------------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 75A-7-102(1): "Assignment" includes any written stock power, bond power, bill of sale, deed, declaration of trust or other instrument of transfer.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-7-102(2): "Claim of beneficial interest" includes:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-7-102(2)(a): a claim of any interest by a decedent's legatee, distributee, heir or creditor, a beneficiary under a trust, a ward, a beneficial owner of a security registered in the name of a nominee, or a minor owner of a security registered in the name of a custodian, or a claim of any similar interest, whether the claim is asserted by the claimant or by a fiduciary or by any other authorized person in his behalf; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-7-102(2)(b): a claim that the transfer would be in breach of fiduciary duties.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-7-102(3): "Corporation" means a private or public corporation, association or trust issuing a security.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-7-102(4): "Fiduciary" means an executor, administrator, trustee, guardian, committee, conservator, curator, tutor, custodian or nominee.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-7-102(5): "Person" includes an individual, a corporation, government or governmental subdivision or agency, business trust, estate, trust, partnership or association, two or more persons having a joint or common interest, or any other legal or commercial entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-7-102(6): "Security" includes any share of stock, bond, debenture, note or other security issued by a corporation which is registered as to ownership on the books of the corporation.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-7-102(7): "Transfer" means a change on the books of a corporation in the registered ownership of a security.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-7-102(8): "Transfer agent" means a person employed or authorized by a corporation to transfer securities issued by the corporation.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-7-103 Registration of security in the name of a fiduciary.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
A corporation or transfer agent registering a security in the name of a person who is a fiduciary or who is described as a fiduciary is not bound to inquire into the existence, extent, or correct description of the fiduciary relationship, and thereafter the corporation and its transfer agent may assume without inquiry that the newly registered owner continues to be the fiduciary until the corporation or transfer agent receives written notice that the fiduciary is no longer acting as such with respect to the particular security.

Utah Code Annotated § 75A-7-104 Assignment of security by a fiduciary.
----------------------------------------------------------------------
Except as otherwise provided in this chapter, a corporation or transfer agent making a transfer of a security pursuant to an assignment by a fiduciary:Utah Code Annotated § 75A-7-104(1): may assume without inquiry that the assignment, even though to the fiduciary himself or to his nominee, is within his authority and capacity and is not in breach of his fiduciary duties;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-7-104(2): may assume without inquiry that the fiduciary has complied with any controlling instrument and with the law of the jurisdiction governing the fiduciary relationship, including any law requiring the fiduciary to obtain court approval of the transfer; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-7-104(3): is not charged with notice of and is not bound to obtain or examine any court record or any recorded or unrecorded document relating to the fiduciary relationship or the assignment, even though the record or document is in its possession.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-7-105 Assignment of security by a fiduciary -- Evidence of appointment or incumbency.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-7-105(1): A corporation or transfer agent making a transfer pursuant to an assignment by a fiduciary who is not the registered owner shall obtain the following evidence of appointment or incumbency:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-7-105(1)(a): in the case of a fiduciary appointed or qualified by a court, a certificate issued by or under the direction or supervision of that court or an officer thereof and dated within 60 days before the transfer; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-7-105(1)(b): in any other case, a copy of a document showing the appointment or a certificate issued by or on behalf of a person reasonably believed by the corporation or transfer agent to be responsible or, in the absence of such a document or certificate, other evidence reasonably deemed by the corporation or transfer agent to be appropriate.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-7-105(2): Corporations and transfer agents may adopt standards with respect to evidence of appointment or incumbency under this subsection provided such standards are not manifestly unreasonable.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-7-105(3): Neither the corporation nor transfer agent is charged with notice of the contents of any document obtained pursuant to this subsection except to the extent that the contents relate directly to the appointment or incumbency.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-7-106 Adverse claims to transfer of security by a fiduciary -- Notice.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-7-106(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-7-106(1)(a): A person asserting a claim of beneficial interest adverse to the transfer of a security pursuant to an assignment by a fiduciary may give the corporation or transfer agent written notice of the claim.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-7-106(1)(b): The corporation or transfer agent is not put on notice unless the written notice identifies the claimant, the registered owner and the issue of which the security is a part, provides an address for communications directed to the claimant and is received before the transfer.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-7-106(1)(c): Nothing in this chapter relieves the corporation or transfer agent of any liability for making or refusing to make the transfer after it is so put on notice, unless it proceeds in the manner authorized in Subsection (2).
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-7-106(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-7-106(2)(a): As soon as practicable after the presentation of a security for transfer pursuant to an assignment by a fiduciary, a corporation or transfer agent which has received notice of a claim of beneficial interest adverse to the transfer may send notice of the presentation by registered or certified mail to the claimant at the address given by him.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-7-106(2)(b): If the corporation or transfer agent so mails such a notice it shall withhold the transfer for 30 days after the mailing and shall then make the transfer unless restrained by a court order.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-7-107 Nonliability of corporation or transfer agent.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
A corporation or transfer agent incurs no liability to any person by making a transfer or otherwise acting in a manner authorized by this chapter.

Utah Code Annotated § 75A-7-108 Nonliability of third persons.
--------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-7-108(1): A person who participates in the acquisition, disposition, assignment or transfer of a security by or to a fiduciary, including a person who guarantees the signature of the fiduciary, is not liable for participation in any breach of fiduciary duty by reason of failure to inquire whether the transaction involves such a breach unless it is shown that the person acted with actual knowledge that the proceeds of the transaction were being or were to be used wrongfully for the individual benefit of the fiduciary or that the transaction was otherwise in breach of duty.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-7-108(2): If a corporation or transfer agent makes a transfer pursuant to an assignment by a fiduciary, a person who guaranteed the signature of the fiduciary is not liable on the guarantee to any person to whom the corporation or transfer agent by reason of this chapter incurs no liability.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-7-108(3): This section does not impose any liability upon the corporation or the corporation's transfer agent.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-7-109 Territorial application of law to rights and duties of corporation or third persons.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-7-109(1): The rights and duties of a corporation and the corporation's transfer agents in registering a security in the name of a fiduciary or in making a transfer of a security pursuant to an assignment by a fiduciary are governed by the law of the jurisdiction under whose laws the corporation is organized.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-7-109(2): This chapter applies to the rights and duties of a person other than the corporation and its transfer agents with regard to acts and omissions in this state in connection with the acquisition, disposition, assignment, or transfer of a security by or to a fiduciary and of a person who guarantees in this state the signature of a fiduciary in connection with such a transaction.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-7-110 Tax obligations not affected .
--------------------------------------------------------------
This chapter does not affect any obligation of a corporation or transfer agent with respect to estate, inheritance, succession or other taxes imposed by the laws of this state.

Utah Code Annotated § 75A-7-111 Construction.
---------------------------------------------
This uniform act shall be so construed as to effectuate the act's general purpose to make uniform the law of those states which enact this uniform act.

Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-102 Definitions for chapter.
--------------------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-102(1): "Adult" means an individual who is 21 years old or older.

Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-103 Scope and jurisdiction.
-------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-103(1): 75A-8-110
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-103(1)(a): 75A-8-110 This chapter applies to a transfer that refers to this chapter in the designation under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-103(1)(b): The custodianship created remains subject to this chapter despite a subsequent change in residence of a transferor, the minor, or the custodian, or the removal of custodial property from this state.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-103(2): A person designated as custodian under this chapter is subject to personal jurisdiction in this state regarding any matter relating to the custodianship.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-103(3): A transfer that purports to be made and is valid under the Uniform Transfers to Minors Act, the Uniform Gifts to Minors Act, or a substantially similar act of another state is governed by the laws of the designated state and may be executed and is enforceable in this state if at the time of the transfer, the transferor, the minor, or the custodian is a resident of the designated state, or the custodial property is located in the designated state.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-104 Nomination of custodian.
--------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-104(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-104(1)(a): A person having the right to designate the recipient of property transferable upon the occurrence of a future event may revocably nominate a custodian to receive the property for a minor beneficiary upon the occurrence of the event by naming the custodian followed in substance by the words: "as custodian for ...............  (name of minor) under the Uniform Transfers to Minors Act."
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-104(1)(b): The nomination may name one or more persons as substitute custodians to whom the property must be transferred, in the order named, if the first nominated custodian dies before the transfer or is unable, declines, or is ineligible to serve.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-104(1)(c): The nomination may be made in a will, a trust, a deed, an instrument exercising a power of appointment, or in a writing designating a beneficiary of contractual rights which is registered with or delivered to the payor, issuer, or other obligor of the contractual rights.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-104(2): 75A-8-110 A custodian nominated under this section must be a person to whom a transfer of property of that kind may be made under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-104(3): 75A-8-110; 75A-8-110
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-104(3)(a): 75A-8-110 The nomination of a custodian under this section does not create custodial property until the nominating instrument becomes irrevocable or a transfer to the nominated custodian is completed under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-104(3)(b): 75A-8-110 Unless the nomination of a custodian has been revoked, upon the occurrence of the future event the custodianship becomes effective and the custodian shall enforce a transfer of the custodial property under Section


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-105 Transfer by gift or exercise of power of appointment.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
A person may make a transfer by irrevocable gift to, or the irrevocable exercise of a power of appointment in favor of, a custodian for the benefit of a minor under Section

Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-106(3): 75A-8-104; 75A-8-110 If the testator or settlor has not nominated a custodian under Section


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-107 Other transfer by fiduciary.

Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-107(1): 75A-8-110 Subject to Subsection (3), a personal representative or trustee may make an irrevocable transfer to another adult or trust company as custodian for the benefit of a minor under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-107(2): 75A-8-110 Subject to Subsection (3), a conservator may make an irrevocable transfer to another adult or trust company as custodian for the benefit of the minor pursuant to Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-107(3): 75A-8-110; 75-1-201 A transfer under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-107(3)(a): the personal representative, trustee, or conservator considers the transfer to be in the best interest of the minor;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-107(3)(b): 75-1-201 the transfer is not prohibited by or inconsistent with provisions of the applicable will, trust agreement, or other governing instrument, as defined in Section

Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-109 Receipt for custodial property.
---------------------------------------------------------------
A written acknowledgment of delivery by a custodian is sufficient receipt and discharge for custodial property transferred to the custodian under this chapter.

Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-110 Manner of creating custodial property and effecting transfer -- Designation of initial custodian -- Control.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
I, ............... (name of transferor or name and representative capacity if a fiduciary) hereby transfer to ............... (name of custodian), as custodian for ............... (name of minor) under the Uniform Transfers to Minors Act, the following: (insert a description of the custodial property sufficient to identify it).Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-110(1): Custodial property is created and a transfer is made when:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-110(1)(a): an uncertificated security or a certificated security in registered form is either:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-110(1)(a)(i): registered in the name of the transferor, an adult other than the transferor, or a trust company, followed in substance by the words: "as custodian for ...............  (name of minor) under the Uniform Transfers to Minors Act"; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-110(1)(a)(ii): delivered if in certificated form, or any document necessary for the transfer of an uncertificated security is delivered, together with any necessary endorsement, to an adult other than the transferor or to a trust company as custodian, accompanied by an instrument in substantially the form in Subsection (2);
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-110(1)(b): money is paid or delivered, or a security held in the name of a broker, financial institution, or its nominee is transferred to a broker, or financial institution for credit to an account in the name of the transferor, an adult other than the transferor, or a trust company, followed in substance by the words: "as custodian for ...............  (name of minor) under the Uniform Transfers to Minors Act";
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-110(1)(c): the ownership of a life or endowment insurance policy or annuity contract is either:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-110(1)(c)(i): registered with the issuer in the name of the transferor, an adult other than the transferor, or a trust company, followed in substance by the words: "as custodian for ...............  (name of minor) under the Uniform Transfers to Minors Act"; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-110(1)(c)(ii): assigned in a writing delivered to an adult other than the transferor or to a trust company whose name in the assignment is followed in substance by the words: "as custodian for ...............  (name of minor) under the Uniform Transfers to Minors Act";
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-110(1)(d): an irrevocable exercise of a power of appointment or an irrevocable present right to future payment under a contract is the subject of a written notification delivered to the payor, issuer, or other obligor that the right is transferred to the transferor, an adult other than the transferor, or a trust company, whose name in the notification is followed in substance by the words: "as custodian for ...............  (name of minor) under the Uniform Transfers to Minors Act";
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-110(1)(e): an interest in real property is recorded in the name of the transferor, an adult other than the transferor, or a trust company, followed in substance by the words: "as custodian for ...............  (name of minor) under the Uniform Transfers to Minors Act";
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-110(1)(f): a certificate of title issued by a department or agency of a state or of the United States which evidences title to tangible personal property is either:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-110(1)(f)(i): issued in the name of the transferor, an adult other than the transferor, or a trust company, followed in substance by the words: "as custodian for ...............  (name of minor) under the Uniform Transfers to Minors Act"; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-110(1)(f)(ii): delivered to an adult other than the transferor or to a trust company, endorsed to that person followed in substance by the words: "as custodian for ...............  (name of minor) under the Uniform Transfers to Minors Act";
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-110(1)(g): an interest in any property not described in Subsections (1)(a) through (f) is transferred to an adult other than the transferor or to a trust company by a written instrument in substantially the form set forth in Subsection (2); or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-110(1)(h): contributions are made into a custodial account at the Utah Educational Savings Plan in accordance with Title 53B, Chapter 8a, Utah Educational Savings Plan.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-110(2): An instrument in the following form satisfies the requirements of Subsections (1)(a)(ii) and (1)(g):  "Transfer Under the Uniform Transfers to Minors Act
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-110(3): A transferor shall place the custodian in control of the custodial property as soon as practicable.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-111 Single custodianship.
-----------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-111(1): A transfer may be made only for one minor, and only one person may be the custodian.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-111(2): All custodial property held under this chapter by the same custodian for the benefit of the same minor constitutes a single custodianship.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-112 Validity and effect of transfer.
----------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-112(1): 75A-8-110; 75A-8-110; 75A-8-104; 75A-8-110 The validity of a transfer made in a manner prescribed in this chapter is not affected by:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-112(1)(a): 75A-8-110 failure of the transferor to comply with Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-112(1)(b): 75A-8-110 designation of an ineligible custodian, except designation of the transferor in the case of property for which the transferor is ineligible to serve as custodian under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-112(1)(c): 75A-8-104; 75A-8-110 death or incapacity of a person nominated under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-112(2): 75A-8-110
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-112(2)(a): 75A-8-110 A transfer made under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-112(2)(b): A minor, or a minor's representative, does not have any right, power, duty, or authority regarding the custodial property except as provided in this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-112(3): By making a transfer, the transferor incorporates in the disposition all the provisions of this chapter and grants to the custodian, and to any third person dealing with a person designated as custodian, the respective powers, rights, and immunities provided in this chapter.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-113 Care of custodial property.
-----------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-113(1): A custodian shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-113(1)(a): take control of custodial property;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-113(1)(b): register or record title to custodial property if appropriate; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-113(1)(c): collect, hold, manage, invest, and reinvest custodial property.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-113(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-113(2)(a): In dealing with custodial property, a custodian shall observe the standard of care that would be observed by a prudent person dealing with property of another and is not limited by any other statute restricting investments by fiduciaries.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-113(2)(b): If a custodian has a special skill or expertise or is named custodian on the basis of representations of a special skill or expertise, the custodian shall use the skill or expertise.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-113(2)(c): However, a custodian may, in the custodian's discretion and without liability to the minor or the minor's estate, retain any custodial property received from a transferor.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-113(3): A custodian may invest in or pay premiums on life insurance or endowment policies on:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-113(3)(a): the life of the minor only if the minor or the minor's estate is the sole beneficiary; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-113(3)(b): the life of another person in whom the minor has an insurable interest only to the extent the minor, the minor's estate, or the custodian in the capacity of custodian, is the irrevocable beneficiary.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-113(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-113(4)(a): A custodian shall at all times keep custodial property separate and distinct from all other property in a manner sufficient to identify it clearly as custodial property of the minor.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-113(4)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-113(4)(b)(i): Custodial property consisting of an undivided interest is so identified if the minor's interest is held as a tenant in common and is fixed.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-113(4)(b)(ii): Custodial property subject to recordation is so identified if it is recorded, and custodial property subject to registration is so identified if it is either registered, or held in an account designated, in the name of the custodian, followed in substance by the words: "as a custodian for ...............  (name of minor) under the Uniform Transfers to Minors Act."
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-113(5): A custodian shall keep records of all transactions with respect to custodial property, including information necessary for the preparation of the minor's tax returns, and shall make them available for inspection at reasonable intervals by a parent or legal representative of the minor or by the minor if the minor is 14 years old or older.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-114 Powers of custodian.
----------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-114(1): A custodian, acting in a custodial capacity, has all the rights, powers, and authority over custodial property that unmarried adult owners have over their own property, but a custodian may exercise those rights, powers, and authority in that capacity only.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-114(2): 75A-8-113 This section does not relieve a custodian from liability for breach of Section


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-115 Use of custodial property.
----------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-115(1): A custodian may deliver or pay to the minor or expend for the minor's benefit so much of the custodial property as the custodian considers advisable for the use and benefit of the minor, without court order and without regard to:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-115(1)(a): the duty or ability of the custodian personally or of any other person to support the minor; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-115(1)(b): any other income or property of the minor which may be applicable or available for that purpose.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-115(2): On petition of an interested person, or the minor if the minor is 14 years old or older, the court may order the custodian to deliver or pay to the minor or expend for the minor's benefit so much of the custodial property as the court considers advisable for the use and benefit of the minor.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-115(3): A delivery, payment, or expenditure under this section is in addition to, not in substitution for, and does not affect any obligation of a person to support the minor.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-116 Custodian's expenses, compensation, and bond.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-116(1): A custodian is entitled to reimbursement from custodial property for reasonable expenses incurred in the performance of the custodian's duties.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-116(2): 75A-8-105 Except for one who is a transferor under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-116(3): 75A-8-119 Except as provided in Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-117 Exemption of third person from liability.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------
A third person in good faith and without court order may act on the instructions of or otherwise deal with any person purporting to make a transfer or purporting to act in the capacity of a custodian and, in the absence of knowledge, is not responsible for determining:Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-117(1): the validity of the purported custodian's designation;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-117(2): the propriety of, or the authority under this chapter for, any act of the purported custodian;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-117(3): the validity or propriety under this chapter of any instrument or instructions executed or given either by the person purporting to make transfer or by the purported custodian; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-117(4): the propriety of the application of any property of the minor delivered to the purported custodian.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-118 Liability to third persons.
-----------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-118(1): A claim may be asserted against the custodial property by proceeding against the custodian in the custodial capacity, whether or not the custodian or the minor is personally liable, if the claim is based on:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-118(1)(a): a contract entered into by a custodian acting in a custodial capacity;
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-118(1)(b): an obligation arising from the ownership or control of custodial property; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-118(1)(c): a tort committed during the custodianship.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-118(2): A custodian is not personally liable:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-118(2)(a): on a contract properly entered into in the custodial capacity unless the custodian fails to reveal that capacity and to identify the custodianship in the contract; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-118(2)(b): for an obligation arising from control of custodial property or for a tort committed during the custodianship unless the custodian is personally at fault.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-118(3): A minor is not personally liable for an obligation arising from ownership of custodial property or for a tort committed during the custodianship unless the minor is personally at fault.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-119 Renunciation, resignation, death, or removal of custodian -- Designation of successor custodian.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-119(1): 75A-8-104; 75A-8-110; 75A-8-104; 75A-8-104; 75A-8-110

Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-119(1)(b): 75A-8-104; 75A-8-104; 75A-8-110 If the event giving rise to a transfer has not occurred and no substitute custodian able, willing, and eligible to serve was nominated under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-119(1)(c): The custodian designated has the rights of a successor custodian.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-119(2): 75A-8-105
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-119(2)(a): 75A-8-105 A custodian at any time may designate a trust company or an adult other than a transferor under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-119(2)(b): If the instrument of designation does not contain or is not accompanied by the resignation of the custodian, the designation of the successor does not take effect until the custodian resigns, dies, becomes incapacitated, or is removed.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-119(3): A custodian may resign at any time by delivering written notice to the minor if the minor is 14 years old or older and to the successor custodian and by delivering the custodial property to the successor custodian.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-119(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-119(4)(a): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-119(4)(a)(i): If a custodian is ineligible, dies, or becomes incapacitated without having effectively designated a successor and the minor is 14 years old or older, the minor may designate as successor custodian, in the manner prescribed in Subsection (2), an adult member of the minor's family, a conservator of the minor, or a trust company.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-119(4)(a)(ii): If the minor is not yet 14 years old or fails to act within 60 days after the ineligibility, death, or incapacity, the conservator of the minor becomes successor custodian.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-119(4)(b): If the minor has no conservator or the conservator declines to act, the transferor, the legal representative of the transferor or of the custodian, an adult member of the minor's family, or any other interested person may petition the court to designate a successor custodian.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-119(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-119(5)(a): A custodian who declines to serve under Subsection (1) or resigns under Subsection (3), or the legal representative of a deceased or incapacitated custodian shall as soon as practicable place the custodial property and records in the possession and control of the successor custodian.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-119(5)(b): The successor custodian by action may enforce the obligation to deliver custodial property and records and becomes responsible for each item as received.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-119(6): 75A-8-105 A transferor, the legal representative of a transferor, an adult member of the minor's family, a guardian of the person of the minor, the conservator of the minor, or the minor if the minor is 14 years old or older, may petition the court to remove the custodian for cause and to designate a successor custodian other than a transferor under Section


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-120 Accounting by and determination of liability of custodian.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-120(1): 75A-8-118 A minor who is 14 years old or older, the minor's guardian of the person or legal representative, an adult member of the minor's family, a transferor, or a transferor's legal representative may petition the court:
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-120(1)(a): for an accounting by the custodian or the custodian's legal representative; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-120(1)(b): 75A-8-118 for a determination of responsibility, as between the custodial property and the custodian personally, for claims against the custodial property unless the responsibility has been adjudicated in an action under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-120(2): A successor custodian may petition the court for an accounting by the predecessor custodian.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-120(3): The court, in a proceeding under this chapter or in any other proceeding, may require or permit the custodian or the custodian's legal representative to account.

Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-121 Termination of custodianship.
-------------------------------------------------------------
The custodian shall transfer in an appropriate manner the custodial property to the minor or to the minor's estate upon the earlier of:Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-121(1): 75A-8-105; 75A-8-106 the minor's becoming 21 years old with respect to custodial property transferred under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-121(2): 75A-8-107; 75A-8-108 the minor's attainment of majority under the laws of this state with respect to the custodial property transferred under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-121(3): the minor's death.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-122 Applicability.
----------------------------------------------
This chapter applies to a transfer within the scope of SectionUtah Code Annotated § 75A-8-122(1): the transfer purports to have been made under the Uniform Gifts to Minors Act; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-122(2): the instrument by which the transfer purports to have been made uses in substance the designation "as custodian under the Uniform Gifts to Minors Act" or "as custodian under the Uniform Transfers to Minors Act" of any other state, and the application of this part is necessary to validate the transfer.


Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-123 Effect on existing custodianships.
------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-123(1): Any transfer of custodial property as now defined in this chapter made before July 1, 1990, is validated notwithstanding that there was no specific authority in the Uniform Gifts to Minors Act for the coverage of custodial property of that kind or for a transfer from that source at the time the transfer was made.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-123(2): This chapter applies to all transfers made before July 1, 1990, in a manner and form prescribed in the Uniform Gifts to Minors Act, except as the application impairs constitutionally vested rights or extends the duration of custodianships in existence on July 1, 1990.
Utah Code Annotated § 75A-8-123(3): 75A-8-102; 75A-8-121 Sections
